It would be finalized in 1962 and is still active today.<sup id="cite_ref-Strasbourg_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Strasbourg-117">[111]</a></sup> Klett's Stuttgart saw two major media events: the same year the partnership with Strasbourg was finalized, then <a href="/wiki/President_of_France" title="President of France">French president</a> Charles de Gaulle visited the city and <a href="/wiki/Ludwigsburg_Palace" title="Ludwigsburg Palace">Ludwigsburg Palace</a> in the ending moments of his state visit to Germany,<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[112]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Queen_Elizabeth_II" class="mw-redirect" title="Queen Elizabeth II">Queen Elizabeth II</a> of the United Kingdom visited the city 24 May <a href="/wiki/1965_in_Germany" title="1965 in Germany">1965</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[113]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 25 April <a href="/wiki/1952_in_Germany" title="1952 in Germany">1952</a>, the other two parts of the former German states of <a href="/wiki/Baden" title="Baden">Baden</a> and <a href="/wiki/W%C3%BCrttemberg" title="Württemberg">Württemberg</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Baden" title="South Baden">South Baden</a> and <a href="/wiki/W%C3%BCrttemberg-Hohenzollern" title="Württemberg-Hohenzollern">Württemberg-Hohenzollern</a> merged and formed the modern German state of <a href="/wiki/Baden-W%C3%BCrttemberg" title="Baden-Württemberg">Baden-Württemberg</a>, with Stuttgart as its capital.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[114]</a></sup> Since the 1950s, Stuttgart has been the third largest city in <a href="/wiki/Southern_Germany" title="Southern Germany">southern Germany</a> behind <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt" title="Frankfurt">Frankfurt</a> and <a href="/wiki/Munich" title="Munich">Munich</a>. The city's population, halved by the Second World War, began sudden growth with the mass influx of <a href="/wiki/Heimatvertriebene" title="Heimatvertriebene">German refugees</a> <a href="/wiki/Flight_and_expulsion_of_Germans_(1944%E2%80%9350)" title="Flight and expulsion of Germans (1944–50)">expelled from their homes and communities</a> by the Soviets from the late 1940s until 1950 to the city. <a href="/wiki/Economic_migrants" class="mw-redirect" title="Economic migrants">Economic migrants</a>, called "<i><a href="/wiki/Gastarbeiter" title="Gastarbeiter">Gastarbeiter</a></i>," from <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a>, and later <a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">Greece</a> and <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a> but primarily from <a href="/wiki/Yugoslavia" title="Yugoslavia">Yugoslavia</a>, came flocking to Stuttgart because of the economic wonder called the "<i><a href="/wiki/Wirtschaftswunder" title="Wirtschaftswunder">Wirtschaftswunder</a></i>" unfolding in <a href="/wiki/West_Germany" title="West Germany">West Germany</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[115]</a></sup> These factors saw the city reach its (then) peak population of 640,000 in 1962.</p>
<p>In the late <a href="/w/index.php?title=1970s_in_Germany&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="1970s in Germany (page does not exist)">1970s</a>, the municipal district of Stammheim was center stage to one of the most controversial periods of German post-war history. <a href="/wiki/Stammheim_Prison" title="Stammheim Prison">Stammheim Prison</a>, built from <a href="/wiki/1959_in_Germany" title="1959 in Germany">1959</a> to <a href="/wiki/1963_in_Germany" title="1963 in Germany">1963</a>, came to be the place of incarceration for <a href="/wiki/Ulrike_Meinhof" title="Ulrike Meinhof">Ulrike Meinhof</a>, <a href="/wiki/Andreas_Baader" title="Andreas Baader">Andreas Baader</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gudrun_Ensslin" title="Gudrun Ensslin">Gudrun Ensslin</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Jan-Carl_Raspe" title="Jan-Carl Raspe">Jan-Carl Raspe</a>, members of a communist terrorist organization known as the <a href="/wiki/Red_Army_Faction" title="Red Army Faction">Red Army Faction</a>, during <a href="/w/index.php?title=Stammheim_trials&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Stammheim trials (page does not exist)">their trial</a> at the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Oberlandesgericht_Stuttgart&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Oberlandesgericht Stuttgart (page does not exist)">Oberlandesgericht Stuttgart</a> in <a href="/wiki/1975_in_Germany" title="1975 in Germany">1975</a>. Several attempts were made by the organization to free the terrorists during the "<a href="/wiki/German_Autumn" title="German Autumn">German Autumn</a>" of <a href="/wiki/1977_in_Germany" title="1977 in Germany">1977</a> that culminated in such events as the <a href="/wiki/Kidnapping_and_murder_of_Hanns-Martin_Schleyer" title="Kidnapping and murder of Hanns-Martin Schleyer">kidnap and murder</a> of <a href="/wiki/Hanns-Martin_Schleyer" class="mw-redirect" title="Hanns-Martin Schleyer">Hanns-Martin Schleyer</a> and the hijacking of <a href="/wiki/Lufthansa_Flight_181" title="Lufthansa Flight 181">Lufthansa Flight 181</a>. When it became clear, after many attempts to free the inmates including the smuggling of three weapons into the prison by their lawyer,<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[116]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[117]</a></sup> that the terrorists could not escape and that they would receive <a href="/wiki/Life_sentence" class="mw-redirect" title="Life sentence">Life sentencing</a>, the terrorists killed themselves<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[g]</a></sup> in April 1977 in an event remembered locally as the "<i>Todesnacht von Stammheim</i>," "Night of Death at Stammheim."</p>
<p>The trauma of the early 1970s was quickly left behind, starting in <a href="/wiki/1974_in_Germany" title="1974 in Germany">1974 in Germany</a> with the <a href="/wiki/1974_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1974 FIFA World Cup">1974 FIFA World Cup</a> and the opening of the <a href="/wiki/Stuttgart_S-Bahn" title="Stuttgart S-Bahn">Stuttgart S-Bahn</a> on 1 October 1978 with a scheduled three routes. from 17 to 19 June 1983, ten European heads of state and representatives from the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> met in Stuttgart for a summit and there made the <a href="/wiki/Solemn_Declaration_on_European_Union" title="Solemn Declaration on European Union">Solemn Declaration on European Union</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[118]</a></sup> Three years later in <a href="/wiki/1986_in_Germany" title="1986 in Germany">1986</a>, the <a href="/wiki/1986_European_Athletics_Championships" title="1986 European Athletics Championships">European Athletics Championships of that year</a> were held in the <a href="/wiki/Mercedes-Benz_Arena_(Stuttgart)" title="Mercedes-Benz Arena (Stuttgart)">Mercedes-Benz Arena</a>. <a href="/wiki/Mikhail_Gorbachev" title="Mikhail Gorbachev">Mikhail Gorbachev</a>, while on a trip to <a href="/wiki/West_Germany" title="West Germany">West Germany</a> to offer a spot for a West German astronaut in a Soviet space mission,<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[119]</a></sup> visited Stuttgart 14 June <a href="/wiki/1989_in_Germany" title="1989 in Germany">1989</a> and was the honored guest of a sumptuous reception held at the <a href="/wiki/New_Palace_(Stuttgart)" title="New Palace (Stuttgart)">Stuttgart</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESauer140_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESauer140-127">[120]</a></sup></p>
<p>Since the monumental happenings of the 1980s, Stuttgart has continued being an important center of not just Europe, but also the world. In <a href="/wiki/1993_in_Germany" title="1993 in Germany">1993</a>, the <a href="/wiki/1993_World_Horticultural_Exposition" title="1993 World Horticultural Exposition">World Horticultural Exposition</a>, for which two new bridges were built,<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[121]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/1993_World_Championships_in_Athletics" title="1993 World Championships in Athletics">World Athletics Championships</a> of that year took place in Stuttgart in the Killesburg park and Mercedes-Benz Area respectively, bringing millions of new visitors to the city. At the 1993 WCA, British athlete <a href="/wiki/Sally_Gunnell" title="Sally Gunnell">Sally Gunnell</a> and the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> Relay team <a href="/wiki/1993_in_athletics_(track_and_field)#World_records" title="1993 in athletics (track and field)">both set world records</a>. In <a href="/wiki/2003_in_Germany" title="2003 in Germany">2003</a>, Stuttgart applied for the <a href="/wiki/2012_Summer_Olympics" title="2012 Summer Olympics">2012 Summer Olympics</a> but failed in their bid when the German Committee for the Olympics decided on <a href="/wiki/Leipzig" title="Leipzig">Leipzig</a> to host the Olympics in Germany. Three years later, in <a href="/wiki/2006_in_Germany" title="2006 in Germany">2006</a>, Stuttgart once again hosted the <a href="/wiki/2006_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2006 FIFA World Cup">FIFA World Cup</a> as it had in 1974.</p>
<p>Stuttgart still experienced some growing pains even long after its recovery from the Second World War. In 2010, the inner city become the focal point of the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Protest_against_Stuttgart_21&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Protest against Stuttgart 21 (page does not exist)">protests against the controversial</a> <a href="/wiki/Stuttgart_21" title="Stuttgart 21">Stuttgart 21f</a>. During the <a href="/wiki/New_Year%27s_Eve_sexual_assaults_in_Germany" title="New Year's Eve sexual assaults in Germany">sexual assaults perpetrated by gangs of migrant men across Germany</a> in 2016, at least 72 complaints were filed to city police of which 17 were sexual assault reports.<sup id="cite_ref-FAZ2_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FAZ2-129">[122]</a></sup> One assailant, a 20 year old asylum seeker from <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a>, was detained for the sexual assaults of two girls as part of a group of other participants in the attacks.<sup id="cite_ref-FAZ2_129-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FAZ2-129">[122]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="US_Military_in_Stuttgart">US Military in Stuttgart</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stuttgart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: US Military in Stuttgart">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Since shortly after the end of World War&#160;II, there has been a US military presence in Stuttgart. At the height of the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a> over 45,000 Americans were stationed across over 40 installations in and around the city.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[123]</a></sup> Today about 10,000 Americans are stationed on 4 installations representing all branches of service within the <a href="/wiki/Department_of_Defense" class="mw-redirect" title="Department of Defense">Department of Defense</a>, unlike the mostly Army presence of the Occupation and Cold War.</p>
<p>In March 1946 the <a href="/wiki/US_Army" class="mw-redirect" title="US Army">US Army</a> established a unit of the <a href="/wiki/US_Constabulary" class="mw-redirect" title="US Constabulary">US Constabulary</a> and a Headquarters at Kurmärker Kaserne (later renamed <a href="/wiki/Patch_Barracks" title="Patch Barracks">Patch Barracks</a>) in Stuttgart. These units of soldiers retrained in patrol and policing provided the law and order in the American zone of occupied Germany until the civilian German police forces could be re-established.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[124]</a></sup> In 1948 the Headquarters for all Constabulary forces was moved to Stuttgart.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[125]</a></sup> In 2008 a memorial to the US Constabulary was installed and dedicated at Patch Barracks.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[126]</a></sup> The US Constabulary headquarters was disbanded in 1950 and most of the force was merged into the newly organized <a href="/wiki/Seventh_Army_(United_States)" class="mw-redirect" title="Seventh Army (United States)">7th Army</a>. As the Cold War developed US Army <a href="/wiki/VII_Corps_(United_States)" title="VII Corps (United States)">VII Corps</a> was re-formed in July 1950 and assigned to Hellenen Kaserne (renamed <a href="/wiki/Kelley_Barracks" title="Kelley Barracks">Kelley Barracks</a> in 1951) where the headquarters was to remain throughout the Cold War.</p>
<p>In 1990 VII Corps was deployed directly from Germany to <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a> for Operations <a href="/wiki/Desert_Shield" class="mw-redirect" title="Desert Shield">Desert Shield</a> and <a href="/wiki/Desert_Storm" class="mw-redirect" title="Desert Storm">Desert Storm</a> to include many of the VII Corps troops stationed in and around Stuttgart. After returning from the Middle East, the bulk of VII Corps units were reassigned to the United States or deactivated. The VII Corps Headquarters returned to Germany for a short period to close out operations and was deactivated later in the United States. The withdrawal of VII Corps caused a large reduction in the US military presence in the city and region and led to the closure of the majority of US installations in and around Stuttgart which resulted in the layoff of many local civilians who had been career employees of the US Army.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[127]</a></sup></p>
<p>Since 1967, Patch Barracks in Stuttgart has been home to the US <a href="/wiki/United_States_European_Command" title="United States European Command">EUCOM</a>. In 2007 <a href="/wiki/United_States_Africa_Command" title="United States Africa Command">AFRICOM</a> was established as a cell within EUCOM and in 2008 established as the US <a href="/wiki/Unified_Combatant_Command" class="mw-redirect" title="Unified Combatant Command">Unified Combatant Command</a> responsible for most of Africa headquartered at Kelley Barracks.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[128]</a></sup> Due to these 2 major headquarters, Stuttgart has been identified as one of the few "enduring communities" where the United States forces will continue to operate in Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[129]</a></sup> The remaining U.S. bases around Stuttgart are organized into US Army Garrison Stuttgart and include Patch Barracks, <a href="/wiki/Robinson_Barracks" title="Robinson Barracks">Robinson Barracks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Panzer_Kaserne" title="Panzer Kaserne">Panzer Kaserne</a> and Kelley Barracks.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[130]</a></sup> From the end of <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> until the early 1990s these installations excepting Patch were almost exclusively Army, but have become increasingly "Purple"—as in joint service—since the end of the Cold War as they are host to <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Defense" title="United States Department of Defense">United States Department of Defense</a> Unified Commands and supporting activities.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[131]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stuttgart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/w/index.php?title=Geography_of_Stuttgart&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Geography of Stuttgart (page does not exist)">Geography of Stuttgart</a></div>
<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right:auto; overflow:hidden; width:auto; max-width:2008px;">
<div class="thumbinner" style="">
<div class="overflowbugx" style="overflow:auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Stuttgart_Panorama_2007.jpg" class="image" title="Panorama of Stuttgart looking southeast. From the Neckar valley on the left the city rises to the city center, backed by high woods to the south (television tower). Stuttgart South and Stuttgart West are to the right."><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Stuttgart_Panorama_2007.jpg/2000px-Stuttgart_Panorama_2007.jpg" width="2000" height="223" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Stuttgart_Panorama_2007.jpg/3000px-Stuttgart_Panorama_2007.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Stuttgart_Panorama_2007.jpg/4000px-Stuttgart_Panorama_2007.jpg 2x" data-file-width="15728" data-file-height="1752" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Stuttgart_Panorama_2007.jpg" title="File:Stuttgart Panorama 2007.jpg"></a></div>
Panorama of Stuttgart looking southeast. From the <a href="/wiki/Neckar" title="Neckar">Neckar</a> valley on the left the city rises to the city center, backed by high woods to the south (<a href="/wiki/Fernsehturm_Stuttgart" title="Fernsehturm Stuttgart">television tower</a>). Stuttgart South and Stuttgart West are to the right.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Stuttgart lies in a fertile bowl-shaped valley about 900 feet (270&#160;m) <a href="/wiki/Above_sea_level" class="mw-redirect" title="Above sea level">above sea level</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTE.27.27EB.27.271911_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTE.27.27EB.27.271911-139">[132]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[h]</a></sup> an hour from the <a href="/wiki/Black_Forest" title="Black Forest">Black Forest</a> and <a href="/wiki/Swabian_Jura" title="Swabian Jura">Swabian Jura</a><sup id="cite_ref-EBStutt_31-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EBStutt-31">[29]</a></sup> on the banks of the <a href="/wiki/Neckar" title="Neckar">Neckar</a> river at <span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="//tools.wmflabs.org/geohack/geohack.php?pagename=Stuttgart&amp;params=48_47_0_N_9_11_0_E_type:city"><span class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">48°47′0″N</span> <span class="longitude">9°11′0″E</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">﻿ / ﻿</span><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">48.78333°N 9.18333°E</span><span style="display:none">﻿ / <span class="geo">48.78333; 9.18333</span></span></span></a></span> 115 miles (185&#160;km) to the west and north of <a href="/wiki/Munich" title="Munich">Munich</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTE.27.27EB.27.271878_141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTE.27.27EB.27.271878-141">[133]</a></sup> The city is often described as being "<i>zwischen Wald und Reben</i>", or "between forest and vines" because of its viticulture and proximity to the nearby forests. Local residents refer to the basin as the <i>Stuttgarter Kessel</i>, or "Stuttgart <a href="/wiki/Cauldron" title="Cauldron">cauldron</a>," during the summer months because of its hot and humid climate that is frequently warmer than the surrounding countryside of <a href="/wiki/W%C3%BCrttemberg" title="Württemberg">Württemberg</a>.</p>
<p>Stuttgart covers an area of 207.35&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (80&#160;sq&#160;mi) and sits at elevation ranging from 207&#160;m (679&#160;ft) <a href="/wiki/Above_mean_sea_level" class="mw-redirect" title="Above mean sea level">above sea level</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Neckar" title="Neckar">Neckar</a> river to 549&#160;m (1,801&#160;ft) on <a href="/wiki/Bernhartsh%C3%B6he" title="Bernhartshöhe">Bernhartshöhe</a> hill – something rather unique in large German cities. The most prominent elevated locales in Stuttgart are the <a href="/wiki/Birkenkopf" title="Birkenkopf">Birkenkopf</a> (511&#160;m (1,677&#160;ft)) on the edge of the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Stuttgart_basin&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Stuttgart basin (page does not exist)">Stuttgart basin</a>, the <a href="/wiki/W%C3%BCrttemberg_(hill)" title="Württemberg (hill)">Württemberg</a> (411&#160;m (1,348&#160;ft)) rising above the Neckar valley, and the <a href="/wiki/Gr%C3%BCner_Heiner" title="Grüner Heiner">Grüner Heiner</a> (395&#160;m (1,296&#160;ft)) at the northeast end of the city.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:RegionStuttgart.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/RegionStuttgart.png/220px-RegionStuttgart.png" width="220" height="155" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/RegionStuttgart.png/330px-RegionStuttgart.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/RegionStuttgart.png/440px-RegionStuttgart.png 2x" data-file-width="1189" data-file-height="839" /></a>

Stuttgart Region with Centers</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Stuttgart is one of 14 <a href="/w/index.php?title=Regional_centers&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Regional centers (page does not exist)">Regional centers</a> in Baden-Württemberg and is naturally the primary center of the <a href="/wiki/Stuttgart_Region" title="Stuttgart Region">Stuttgart Region</a>, making it the administrative center for a region of 3,700 square kilometres (1,400&#160;sq&#160;mi) containing a total of 2.76 million people as of December 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[134]</a></sup> In addition to this, Stuttgart serves as a Mittelzentrum for <a href="/wiki/Esslingen_(district)" title="Esslingen (district)">Esslingen</a> <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_Germany" title="Districts of Germany">District</a> cities <a href="/wiki/Leinfelden-Echterdingen" title="Leinfelden-Echterdingen">Leinfelden-Echterdingen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Filderstadt" title="Filderstadt">Filderstadt</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ditzingen" title="Ditzingen">Ditzingen</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Gerlingen" title="Gerlingen">Gerlingen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Korntal-M%C3%BCnchingen" title="Korntal-Münchingen">Korntal-Münchingen</a> in <a href="/wiki/Ludwigsburg_(district)" title="Ludwigsburg (district)">Ludwigsburg</a> District. Stuttgart is also chief of the three centers <a href="/wiki/Stuttgart_Metropolitan_Region" title="Stuttgart Metropolitan Region">Stuttgart Metropolitan Region</a>, an area of 15,000 square kilometres (5,800&#160;sq&#160;mi) containing 5.3 million persons.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[135]</a></sup></p>
<table class="wikitable">

</tr>
<tr style="background:#fff;">

</tr>
</table>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stuttgart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:StuttgartCentreWinter.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/StuttgartCentreWinter.jpg/220px-StuttgartCentreWinter.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/StuttgartCentreWinter.jpg/330px-StuttgartCentreWinter.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/StuttgartCentreWinter.jpg/440px-StuttgartCentreWinter.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2272" data-file-height="1704" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:StuttgartCentreWinter.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
City center, winter</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Stuttgart experiences an <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_climate" title="Oceanic climate">Oceanic climate</a> (Cfb),<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[136]</a></sup> just like the <a href="/wiki/British_Isles" title="British Isles">British Isles</a> and <a href="/wiki/Northern_France" class="mw-redirect" title="Northern France">Northern France</a>, but it is very extreme at times. As a result of the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Urban_warming&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Urban warming (page does not exist)">urban warming</a> caused by the dense development of the city, inside its "Cauldron" average temperatures in the summer months regularly beat 20&#160;°C (68&#160;°F) from June to August and come very near in September. In the winter temperatures are quite mild, with daily means never sinking below 0&#160;°C (32&#160;°F) even in the coldest months (January and February). In spite of the heat, there is no dry season and the city receives frequent but moderate precipitation year-round. Annually, the city receives 869&#160;mm (34.2&#160;in) of rain (German average national annual rainfall is 700&#160;mm (28&#160;in)).<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[137]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Climate_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Climate-146">[138]</a></sup> On average, Stuttgart enjoys 1,807 hours of sunshine per year and an average annual temperature of 9&#160;°C (48&#160;°F).<sup id="cite_ref-Web_147-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Web-147">[139]</a></sup></p>
<p>Typically during summer months, the nearby hills, <a href="/wiki/Swabian_Alb" class="mw-redirect" title="Swabian Alb">Swabian Alb</a> mountains, and <a href="/wiki/Black_Forest" title="Black Forest">Black Forest</a>, <a href="/wiki/Schurwald" title="Schurwald">Schurwald</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Swabian-Franconian_Forest" title="Swabian-Franconian Forest">Swabian-Franconian Forest</a> act as a shield from harsh weather but the city can be subject to thunderstorms, whereas in the winter periods snow may last for several days. Winters last from December to March. The coldest month is January with an average temperature of 0&#160;°C (32&#160;°F). Snow cover tends to last no longer than a few days although it has been known to last several weeks at a time as recently as 2010. The summers are warm with an average temperature of 20&#160;°C (68&#160;°F) in the hottest months of July and August. Summers last from May until September. Though it is a rare occurrence in Stuttgart, the city sometimes receives damaging <a href="/wiki/Hailstorms" class="mw-redirect" title="Hailstorms">hailstorms</a>, such as in July 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">[140]</a></sup> In order to fight this phenomenon, weather stations known as "<i>Hagelflieger</i>" are stationed near the city and are largely funded by <a href="/wiki/Daimler_AG" title="Daimler AG">Daimler AG</a>, who maintain several parking lots and factories in the municipal area.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[141]</a></sup></p>
<p><br /></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Landmarks_and_culture">Landmarks and culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stuttgart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Landmarks and culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/w/index.php?title=Culture_of_Stuttgart&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Culture of Stuttgart (page does not exist)">Culture of Stuttgart</a></div>
<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right:auto; overflow:hidden; width:auto; max-width:1288px;">
<div class="thumbinner" style="">
<div class="overflowbugx" style="overflow:auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Solitude_pan-pjt.jpg" class="image" title="Solitude Palace"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Solitude_pan-pjt.jpg/1280px-Solitude_pan-pjt.jpg" width="1280" height="377" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Solitude_pan-pjt.jpg/1920px-Solitude_pan-pjt.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Solitude_pan-pjt.jpg/2560px-Solitude_pan-pjt.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5525" data-file-height="1627" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Solitude_pan-pjt.jpg" title="File:Solitude pan-pjt.jpg"></a></div>
Solitude Palace</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_inner_city">The inner city</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stuttgart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: The inner city">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Stiftskirche_Stuttgart.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Stiftskirche_Stuttgart.jpeg/170px-Stiftskirche_Stuttgart.jpeg" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Stiftskirche_Stuttgart.jpeg/255px-Stiftskirche_Stuttgart.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Stiftskirche_Stuttgart.jpeg/340px-Stiftskirche_Stuttgart.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="480" data-file-height="640" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Stiftskirche_Stuttgart.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <i>Stiftskirche</i>, seen from the west (Stiftstraße)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>At the center of Stuttgart lies its main square, <a href="/wiki/Schlossplatz,_Stuttgart" class="mw-redirect" title="Schlossplatz, Stuttgart">Schlossplatz</a>. As well as being the largest square in Stuttgart, it stands at the crossover point between the city's shopping area, <i>Schlossgarten</i> park which runs down to the river <a href="/wiki/Neckar" title="Neckar">Neckar</a>, Stuttgart's two central castles and major museums and residential areas to the south west. Königstraße, Stuttgart's most important shopping street which runs along the northwestern edge of Schlossplatz, claims to be the longest pedestrianized street in Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBekker2005445_152-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBekker2005445-152">[144]</a></sup></p>
<p>Although the city center was heavily damaged during World War II,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBekker2005445_152-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBekker2005445-152">[144]</a></sup> many historic buildings have been reconstructed and the city boasts some fine pieces of modern post-war architecture. Buildings and squares of note in the <a href="/wiki/Inner_city" title="Inner city">inner city</a> include:</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Stuttgart_AlteKanzlei01.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Stuttgart_AlteKanzlei01.JPG/220px-Stuttgart_AlteKanzlei01.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Stuttgart_AlteKanzlei01.JPG/330px-Stuttgart_AlteKanzlei01.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Stuttgart_AlteKanzlei01.JPG/440px-Stuttgart_AlteKanzlei01.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2848" data-file-height="2136" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Stuttgart_AlteKanzlei01.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <i>Alte Kanzlei</i> on <a href="/wiki/Schillerplatz_(Stuttgart)" title="Schillerplatz (Stuttgart)">Schillerplatz</a> square</div>
</div>
</div>
<ul>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Stiftskirche,_Stuttgart" title="Stiftskirche, Stuttgart"><i>Stiftskirche</i></a> (Collegiate Church), dates back to the 12th century, but was changed to the Late Gothic style in the 15th century and has been a Protestant church since 1534.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBekker2005445_152-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBekker2005445-152">[144]</a></sup> Exterior: <a href="/wiki/Romanesque_architecture" title="Romanesque architecture">Romanesque</a>/<a href="/wiki/Gothic_architecture" title="Gothic architecture">Gothic</a>; interior: Romanesque/Gothic/Modern. Reconstructed with simplified interior after World War II.</li>
<li><i>Altes Schloss</i> (the <a href="/wiki/Old_Castle_(Stuttgart)" title="Old Castle (Stuttgart)">Old Castle</a>), mostly dating from the late 15th century, some parts date back to 1320.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBekker2005445_152-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBekker2005445-152">[144]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Renaissance_architecture" title="Renaissance architecture">Renaissance</a> style; reconstructed<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBekker2005445_152-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBekker2005445-152">[144]</a></sup></li>
<li><i>Alte Kanzlei</i> (the Old Chancellery) on <a href="/wiki/Schillerplatz_(Stuttgart)" title="Schillerplatz (Stuttgart)">Schillerplatz</a> square which backs onto the 1598 Mercury Pillar</li>
<li><i>Neues Schloss</i> (the <a href="/wiki/New_Castle_(Stuttgart)" class="mw-redirect" title="New Castle (Stuttgart)">New Castle</a>), completed in 1807.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBekker2005445_152-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBekker2005445-152">[144]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Baroque" title="Baroque">Baroque</a>/<a href="/wiki/Classicism" title="Classicism">Classicism</a>); reconstructed with modern interior, currently houses government offices.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBekker2005445_152-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBekker2005445-152">[144]</a></sup> The cellars with a collection of stone fragments from the Roman times are open to visitors<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">[145]</a></sup></li>
<li><i>Wilhelmpalais</i> (the King <a href="/wiki/Wilhelm_Palais" title="Wilhelm Palais">Wilhelm Palais</a>), 1840</li>
<li><i>Königsbau</i> (the King's Building), 1850. Classicism; reconstructed; has been housing the "Königsbau Passagen" shopping centre since 2006.</li>
<li>The <i>Großes Haus</i> of <a href="/wiki/Staatstheater_Stuttgart" title="Staatstheater Stuttgart">Stuttgart National Theatre</a>, 1909–1912</li>
<li><i>Markthalle</i> Market Hall, 1910. (<a href="/wiki/Art_Nouveau" title="Art Nouveau">Art Nouveau</a>)</li>
<li>The <i><a href="/wiki/Stuttgart_Hauptbahnhof" title="Stuttgart Hauptbahnhof">Hauptbahnhof</a></i> (Main Railway Station) was designed in 1920;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBekker2005445_152-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBekker2005445-152">[144]</a></sup> its stark, functional lines are typical of the artistic trend 'Neue Sachlichkeit' (<a href="/wiki/New_Objectivity" title="New Objectivity">New Objectivity</a>)<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBekker2005445_152-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBekker2005445-152">[144]</a></sup></li>
<li>The <i><a href="/wiki/W%C3%BCrttembergische_Landesbibliothek" title="Württembergische Landesbibliothek">Württembergische Landesbibliothek</a></i> state library, rebuilt in 1970.</li>
<li><i>Friedrichsbau Varieté</i> (Friedrich Building), rebuilt in 1994 on the site of the former art nouveau building</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Architecture_in_other_districts">Architecture in other districts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stuttgart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Architecture in other districts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Stuttgart_Wilhelma_1900.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/83/Stuttgart_Wilhelma_1900.jpg/220px-Stuttgart_Wilhelma_1900.jpg" width="220" height="166" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/83/Stuttgart_Wilhelma_1900.jpg/330px-Stuttgart_Wilhelma_1900.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/83/Stuttgart_Wilhelma_1900.jpg/440px-Stuttgart_Wilhelma_1900.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="483" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Stuttgart_Wilhelma_1900.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Wilhelma" title="Wilhelma">Wilhelma</a> Zoo and Botanical Garden, around 1900</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>A number of significant castles stand in Stuttgart's suburbs and beyond as reminders of the city's royal past. These include:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Castle_Solitude" title="Castle Solitude">Castle Solitude</a>, 1700–1800. Baroque/<a href="/wiki/Rococo" title="Rococo">Rococo</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ludwigsburg_Palace" title="Ludwigsburg Palace">Ludwigsburg Palace</a>, 1704–1758. Baroque, with its enormous baroque garden.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hohenheim" title="Hohenheim">Castle Hohenheim</a>, 1771–1793</li>
</ul>
<p>Other landmarks in and around Stuttgart include (<i>see also <a href="#Museums">museums</a> below):</i></p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Rosenstein_Castle" class="mw-redirect" title="Rosenstein Castle">Castle Rosenstein</a> (1822–1830) Classical</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/W%C3%BCrttemberg_Mausoleum" title="Württemberg Mausoleum">Württemberg Mausoleum</a> (1824) which holds the remains of <a href="/wiki/Catherine_Pavlovna_of_Russia" title="Catherine Pavlovna of Russia">Catherine Pavlovna of Russia</a> and King <a href="/wiki/William_I_of_W%C3%BCrttemberg" title="William I of Württemberg">William I of Württemberg</a></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Wilhelma" title="Wilhelma">Wilhelma</a></i> Zoo and Botanical Gardens (1853)</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Observation_Tower_Burgholzhof" title="Observation Tower Burgholzhof">Observation Tower of Burgholzhof</a> an 1891 brick observation tower constructed by the Cannstatt municipal architect Friedrich Keppler on behalf of the Verschönerungsverein Cannstatt e. V. ("Society for the Beautification of Cannstatt"), in the style of a Roman tower.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Weissenhof_Estate" title="Weissenhof Estate">Weissenhof Estate</a> (1927), (<a href="/wiki/International_Style_(architecture)" title="International Style (architecture)">International Style</a>)</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Fernsehturm_Stuttgart" title="Fernsehturm Stuttgart">TV Tower</a> (1950), the world's first concrete TV tower</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Stuttgart_Airport" title="Stuttgart Airport">Stuttgart Airport</a> Terminal Building, 2000. In neighboring <a href="/wiki/Leinfelden-Echterdingen" title="Leinfelden-Echterdingen">Leinfelden-Echterdingen</a></li>
</ul>
<h3><span id="Parks,_lakes,_cemeteries_and_other_places_of_interest"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Parks.2C_lakes.2C_cemeteries_and_other_places_of_interest">Parks, lakes, cemeteries and other places of interest</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stuttgart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Parks, lakes, cemeteries and other places of interest">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Feuersee_Spring.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Feuersee_Spring.jpg/220px-Feuersee_Spring.jpg" width="220" height="323" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Feuersee_Spring.jpg/330px-Feuersee_Spring.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Feuersee_Spring.jpg/440px-Feuersee_Spring.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2370" data-file-height="3484" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Feuersee_Spring.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Johanneskirche on the Feuersee, designed by <a href="/wiki/Christian_Friedrich_von_Leins" title="Christian Friedrich von Leins">Christian Friedrich von Leins</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Killesbergpark.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Killesbergpark.jpg/170px-Killesbergpark.jpg" width="170" height="271" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Killesbergpark.jpg/255px-Killesbergpark.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Killesbergpark.jpg/340px-Killesbergpark.jpg 2x" data-file-width="400" data-file-height="637" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Killesbergpark.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Killesbergpark" title="Killesbergpark">Killesbergpark</a> with fountains and vineyards in the background</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>At the center of Stuttgart lies a series of gardens which are popular with families and cyclists. Because of its shape on a map, the locals refer to it as the <i>Green U</i>. The Green U starts with the old Schlossgarten, castle gardens first mentioned in records in 1350. The modern park stretches down to the river <a href="/wiki/Neckar" title="Neckar">Neckar</a> and is divided into the upper garden (bordering the <a href="/wiki/Old_Castle_(Stuttgart)" title="Old Castle (Stuttgart)">Old Castle</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Stuttgart_Hauptbahnhof" title="Stuttgart Hauptbahnhof">Main Station</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Staatstheater_Stuttgart" title="Staatstheater Stuttgart">State Theater</a> and the State Parliament building), and the middle and lower gardens – a total of 61 hectares. The park also houses Stuttgart planetarium.</p>
<p>At the far end of Schlossgarten lies the second <i>Green U</i> park, the larger <a href="/wiki/Rosensteinpark" class="mw-redirect" title="Rosensteinpark">Rosensteinpark</a> which borders Stuttgart's <a href="/wiki/Wilhelma" title="Wilhelma">Wilhelma</a> zoo and botanical gardens. Planted by King <a href="/wiki/William_I_of_W%C3%BCrttemberg" title="William I of Württemberg">William I of Württemberg</a>, it contains many old trees and open areas and counts as the largest English-style garden in southern Germany. In the grounds of the park stands the former Rosenstein castle, now the Rosenstein museum.</p>
<p>Beyond bridges over an adjacent main road lies the final <i>Green U</i> park, <a href="/wiki/Killesbergpark" title="Killesbergpark">Killesbergpark</a> or 'Höhenpark' which is a former quarry that was converted for the <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Third Reich</a> garden show of 1939 (and was used as a collection point for Jews awaiting transportation to <a href="/wiki/Internment" title="Internment">concentration camps</a>). The park has been used to stage many gardening shows since the 1950s, including the <a href="/wiki/Bundesgartenschau" title="Bundesgartenschau">Bundesgartenschau</a> and 1993 International Gardening Show, and runs miniature trains all around the park in the summer months for children and adults. The viewing tower (Killesbergturm) offers unique views across to the north east of Stuttgart.</p>
<p>On the northern edge of the <a href="/wiki/Rosensteinpark" class="mw-redirect" title="Rosensteinpark">Rosensteinpark</a> is the famous '<a href="/wiki/Wilhelma" title="Wilhelma">Wilhelma</a>', Germany's only combined zoological and botanical garden. The whole compound, with its ornate pavilions, greenhouses, walls and gardens was built around 1850 as a summer palace in moorish style for King <a href="/wiki/Wilhelm_I,_German_Emperor" class="mw-redirect" title="Wilhelm I, German Emperor">Wilhelm I</a> of <a href="/wiki/W%C3%BCrttemberg" title="Württemberg">Württemberg</a>. It currently houses around 8000 animals and some 5000 plant species and contains the biggest <a href="/wiki/Magnolia" title="Magnolia">magnolia</a> grove in Europe.</p>
<p>Other parks in Stuttgart include the historic <a href="/wiki/Botanischer_Garten_der_Universit%C3%A4t_Hohenheim" class="mw-redirect" title="Botanischer Garten der Universität Hohenheim">Botanischer Garten der Universität Hohenheim</a> and <a href="/wiki/Landesarboretum_Baden-W%C3%BCrttemberg" title="Landesarboretum Baden-Württemberg">Landesarboretum Baden-Württemberg</a> at <a href="/wiki/Hohenheim" title="Hohenheim">Castle Hohenheim</a> (which date back to 1776 and are still used to catalog and research plant species), Uhlandshöhe hill (between the city center, Bad Cannstatt and Frauenkopf, and home to Stuttgart observatory), the Weißenburgpark (a five-hectare park in the Bopser area of Stuttgart South which dates back to 1834 and is now home to a 'tea house' and the 'marble room' and offers a relaxing view across the city center), the <a href="/wiki/Birkenkopf" title="Birkenkopf">Birkenkopf</a> a <a href="/wiki/Schuttberg" title="Schuttberg">Schuttberg</a> (at 511 metres (1,677&#160;ft) the highest point in central Stuttgart, where many ruins were laid to commemorate the Second World War), and the Eichenhain park in Sillenbuch (declared a nature reserve in 1958 and home to 200 <a href="/wiki/Oak" title="Oak">oak</a> trees, many 300–400 years old).</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Birkenkopf_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Birkenkopf_1.jpg/220px-Birkenkopf_1.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Birkenkopf_1.jpg/330px-Birkenkopf_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Birkenkopf_1.jpg/440px-Birkenkopf_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3872" data-file-height="2592" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Birkenkopf_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
View from the Birkenkopf (partly a <a href="/wiki/Schuttberg" title="Schuttberg">Schuttberg</a>)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>There are a number of natural and artificial lakes and ponds in Stuttgart. The largest is the <a href="/wiki/Max-Eyth-See" title="Max-Eyth-See">Max-Eyth-See</a>, which was created in 1935 by reclaiming a former quarry and is now an official nature reserve. It is surrounded by an expansive open area overlooked by vineyards on the banks of the river <a href="/wiki/Neckar" title="Neckar">Neckar</a> near [Mühlhausen]. There are expansive areas of woodland to the west and south west of Stuttgart which are popular with walkers, families, cyclists and ramblers. The most frequented lakes form a 3&#160;km (1.9&#160;mi) trio made up of the Bärensee, Neuer See and Pfaffensee. The lakes are also used for local water supplies.</p>
<p>In the Feuersee area in the west of Stuttgart lies one of two 'Feuersee's (literally fire lakes), striking for its views of the <a href="/wiki/Johanneskirche_(Stuttgart)" class="mw-redirect" title="Johanneskirche (Stuttgart)">Johanneskirche</a> (St. Johns) church across the lake, surrounded by nearby houses and offices. The other Feuersee can be found in Vaihingen.</p>
<p><b>Cemeteries</b> in Stuttgart include:</p>
<ul>
<li>The Hoppenlaufriedhof in Central Stuttgart, the oldest remaining cemetery which dates back to 1626, an <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/infirmary" class="extiw" title="wikt:infirmary">infirmary</a> graveyard last used in 1951</li>
<li>The Waldfriedhof, the 1913 forest cemetery that is connected to Südheimer Platz by <a href="/wiki/Standseilbahn_Stuttgart" title="Standseilbahn Stuttgart">funicular railway</a></li>
<li>The Pragfriedhof, with its <a href="/wiki/Art_Nouveau" title="Art Nouveau">Art Nouveau</a> <a href="/wiki/Cremation" title="Cremation">crematorium</a>. Established in 1873 it was extended to include Jewish graves in 1874 and also now houses the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Orthodox_Church" title="Russian Orthodox Church">Russian Orthodox Church</a> of <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Nevsky" title="Alexander Nevsky">Alexander Nevsky</a></li>
<li>The Uff-Kirchhof cemetery in Bad Cannstatt which stands at the crossroads of two ancient <a href="/wiki/Roman_roads" title="Roman roads">Roman roads</a> and Cannstatter Hauptfriedhof, the largest graveyard in Stuttgart which has been used as a Muslim burial ground since 1985.</li>
</ul>
<p>The city boasts the largest mineral water deposits in Europe after <a href="/wiki/Budapest" title="Budapest">Budapest</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBekker2005445_152-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBekker2005445-152">[144]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Typical_154-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Typical-154">[146]</a></sup> with over 250 springs within the urban area.<sup id="cite_ref-Typical_154-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Typical-154">[146]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture_and_events">Culture and events</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stuttgart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Culture and events">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Stuttgart_Staatsoper.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Stuttgart_Staatsoper.jpg/220px-Stuttgart_Staatsoper.jpg" width="220" height="130" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Stuttgart_Staatsoper.jpg/330px-Stuttgart_Staatsoper.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Stuttgart_Staatsoper.jpg/440px-Stuttgart_Staatsoper.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2629" data-file-height="1559" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Stuttgart_Staatsoper.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Staatstheater_Stuttgart" title="Staatstheater Stuttgart">State Opera House</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Stiftskirche_stuttgart.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Stiftskirche_stuttgart.jpg/170px-Stiftskirche_stuttgart.jpg" width="170" height="232" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Stiftskirche_stuttgart.jpg/255px-Stiftskirche_stuttgart.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Stiftskirche_stuttgart.jpg/340px-Stiftskirche_stuttgart.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2593" data-file-height="3532" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Stiftskirche_stuttgart.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Protestant <a href="/wiki/Stiftskirche_(Stuttgart)" class="mw-redirect" title="Stiftskirche (Stuttgart)">Stiftskirche</a> (originally built in 1170, pictured around 1900) with the memorial on <a href="/wiki/Schillerplatz_(Stuttgart)" title="Schillerplatz (Stuttgart)"><i>Schillerplatz</i></a> square in foreground</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Stuttgart is known for its rich cultural heritage, in particular its <a href="/wiki/Staatstheater_Stuttgart" title="Staatstheater Stuttgart">State Theatre (<i>Staatstheater</i>)</a> and <a href="/wiki/Staatsgalerie_Stuttgart" title="Staatsgalerie Stuttgart">State Gallery (<i>Staatsgalerie</i>)</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Staatstheater_Stuttgart" title="Staatstheater Stuttgart"><i>Staatstheater</i></a> is home to the <a href="/wiki/Staatsoper_Stuttgart" title="Staatsoper Stuttgart">State opera</a> and three smaller theatres and it regularly stages opera, ballet and theatre productions as well as concerts. The <a href="/wiki/Staatstheater_Stuttgart" title="Staatstheater Stuttgart">Staatstheater</a> was named Germany/Austria/Switzerland "Theatre of the year" in 2006; the Stuttgart Opera has won the 'Opera of the year' award six times.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">[147]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Stuttgart_Ballet" title="Stuttgart Ballet">Stuttgart Ballet</a> is connected to names like <a href="/wiki/John_Cranko" title="John Cranko">John Cranko</a> and Marcia Haydée.</p>
<p>Stuttgart is also home to one of Germany's most prestigious <a href="/wiki/Symphony_orchestra" class="mw-redirect" title="Symphony orchestra">symphony orchestras</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Stuttgart_Radio_Symphony_Orchestra" title="Stuttgart Radio Symphony Orchestra">Stuttgart Radio Symphony Orchestra</a>, with famous English conductor <a href="/wiki/Roger_Norrington" title="Roger Norrington">Sir Roger Norrington</a>, who developed a distinct sound of that orchestra, known as the <i>Stuttgart Sound</i>. They mostly perform in the <i>Liederhalle</i> concert hall.</p>
<p>The city offers two Broadway-style musical theaters, the Apollo and the Palladium Theater (each approx. 1800 seats). <a href="/wiki/Ludwigsburg_Palace" title="Ludwigsburg Palace">Ludwigsburg Palace</a> in the nearby town of <a href="/wiki/Ludwigsburg" title="Ludwigsburg">Ludwigsburg</a> is also used throughout the year as a venue for concerts and cultural events.</p>
<p>As a result of Stuttgart's long history of <a href="/wiki/Viticulture" title="Viticulture">viticulture</a> (Even today there are vineyards less than 500&#160;m (1,640&#160;ft) from the <a href="/wiki/Stuttgart_Hauptbahnhof" title="Stuttgart Hauptbahnhof">Main Station</a>), there are more than 400 flights of stairs (known in the local dialect as the "<i>Stäffele</i>") around the city, equivalent to approximately 20&#160;km (12&#160;mi) of steps.<sup id="cite_ref-St.C3.A4ffele_156-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-St.C3.A4ffele-156">[148]</a></sup> Later, in the early 19th Century, the city continued to grow and many vineyards were replaced by houses and streets and the <i>Stäffele</i> were used as foot paths to connect the newly built neighborhoods. Some of the stairs were elaborately decorated with fountains and plantings.<sup id="cite_ref-St.C3.A4ffele_156-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-St.C3.A4ffele-156">[148]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Hanns-Martin-Schleyer-Halle" title="Hanns-Martin-Schleyer-Halle">Schleyerhalle</a> sports arena is regularly used to stage rock and pop concerts with major international stars on European tour.</p>
<p>Stuttgart's Swabian cuisine, beer and wine have been produced in the area since the 17th century and are now famous throughout Germany and beyond.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">[149]</a></sup> For example, <a href="/wiki/Gaisburger_Marsch" title="Gaisburger Marsch">Gaisburger Marsch</a> is a stew that was invented in Stuttgart's Gaisburg area of Stuttgart East.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cannstatter-fruchtsaeule-2004.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Cannstatter-fruchtsaeule-2004.jpg/170px-Cannstatter-fruchtsaeule-2004.jpg" width="170" height="198" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Cannstatter-fruchtsaeule-2004.jpg/255px-Cannstatter-fruchtsaeule-2004.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Cannstatter-fruchtsaeule-2004.jpg/340px-Cannstatter-fruchtsaeule-2004.jpg 2x" data-file-width="400" data-file-height="465" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cannstatter-fruchtsaeule-2004.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Cannstatter_Volksfest" title="Cannstatter Volksfest">Cannstatter Volksfest</a> in the district of 'Bad Cannstatt'</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In October 2009 the Stuttgart Ministry of Agriculture announced that the European Union was to officially recognise the pasta dish <a href="/wiki/Maultasche" title="Maultasche">Maultaschen</a> as a "regional specialty", thus marking its significance to the cultural heritage of <a href="/wiki/Baden-W%C3%BCrttemberg" title="Baden-Württemberg">Baden-Württemberg</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">[150]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1993 Stuttgart hosted the <a href="/wiki/1993_World_Horticultural_Exposition" title="1993 World Horticultural Exposition">International Garden Show</a> in the suburb of <a href="/wiki/Killesbergpark" title="Killesbergpark">Killesberg</a>. In 2006 it was also one of the host cities of the <a href="/wiki/2006_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2006 FIFA World Cup">Football World Cup</a>. In 2007, Stuttgart hosted the <a href="/wiki/2007_World_Artistic_Gymnastics_Championships" title="2007 World Artistic Gymnastics Championships">2007 World Artistic Gymnastics Championships</a>. In 2008 it was host to the <a href="/wiki/World_Individual_Debating_and_Public_Speaking_Championships" title="World Individual Debating and Public Speaking Championships">World Individual Debating and Public Speaking Championships</a>.</p>
<p>Regular events that take place in Stuttgart:</p>
<ul>
<li>The world-famous annual <a href="/wiki/Cannstatter_Volksfest" title="Cannstatter Volksfest">'Volksfest'</a>, originally a traditional agricultural fair which now also hosts beer tents and a French village and is second in size only to the <a href="/wiki/Oktoberfest" title="Oktoberfest">Oktoberfest</a> in Munich. There is also a <a href="/wiki/Stuttgart_Spring_Festival" title="Stuttgart Spring Festival">Spring festival</a> on the same grounds in April of each year.</li>
<li>With more than 3.6 million visitors in 2007<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">[151]</a></sup> and more than 200 stands, Stuttgart's <a href="/wiki/Christmas_Market,_Stuttgart" title="Christmas Market, Stuttgart">Christmas Market</a>, running from late November to 23 December,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChristiani2015311_160-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChristiani2015311-160">[152]</a></sup> is the largest and one of the oldest traditional Christmas markets in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChristiani2015311_160-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChristiani2015311-160">[152]</a></sup> It is especially renowned for its abundant decorations and takes place in the four weeks leading up to Christmas.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">[153]</a></sup></li>
<li>The Fish Market (<i>Hamburger Fischmarkt</i>, late July) with fresh fish, other food and beer from <a href="/wiki/Hamburg" title="Hamburg">Hamburg</a>.</li>
<li>The Summer Festival (<i>Stuttgart Sommerfest</i>, usually in early August) with shows, music, children's entertainment and local cuisine in <a href="/wiki/Schlossplatz,_Stuttgart" class="mw-redirect" title="Schlossplatz, Stuttgart">Schlossplatz, Stuttgart</a><sup id="cite_ref-Peters.2C_p._430_162-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Peters.2C_p._430-162">[154]</a></sup> and adjacent parks</li>
<li>The Lantern Festival (<i>Lichterfest</i>, early July) in <a href="/wiki/Killesbergpark" title="Killesbergpark">Killesberg</a> park with its famous firework display and fairground attractions</li>
<li>The Wine Village (<i>Weindorf</i>, late August/early September) – vintages are sold at this event held at Schlossplatz and Upper Palace Garden<sup id="cite_ref-Peters.2C_p._430_162-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Peters.2C_p._430-162">[154]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Museums">Museums</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stuttgart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Museums">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Stuttgart_alte_staatsgalerie.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Stuttgart_alte_staatsgalerie.jpg/220px-Stuttgart_alte_staatsgalerie.jpg" width="220" height="171" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Stuttgart_alte_staatsgalerie.jpg/330px-Stuttgart_alte_staatsgalerie.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Stuttgart_alte_staatsgalerie.jpg/440px-Stuttgart_alte_staatsgalerie.jpg 2x" data-file-width="713" data-file-height="555" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Stuttgart_alte_staatsgalerie.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Entrance to the <a href="/wiki/Staatsgalerie_Stuttgart" title="Staatsgalerie Stuttgart">Old State Gallery</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:W%C3%BCrttembergische_K%C3%B6nigskrone.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/W%C3%BCrttembergische_K%C3%B6nigskrone.jpg/170px-W%C3%BCrttembergische_K%C3%B6nigskrone.jpg" width="170" height="193" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/W%C3%BCrttembergische_K%C3%B6nigskrone.jpg/255px-W%C3%BCrttembergische_K%C3%B6nigskrone.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/W%C3%BCrttembergische_K%C3%B6nigskrone.jpg/340px-W%C3%BCrttembergische_K%C3%B6nigskrone.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2157" data-file-height="2448" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:W%C3%BCrttembergische_K%C3%B6nigskrone.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/W%C3%BCrttemberg" title="Württemberg">Württemberg</a> crown jewels on display in the State Museum of Württemberg (<a href="/wiki/Old_Castle_(Stuttgart)" title="Old Castle (Stuttgart)">Old Castle</a>)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Stuttgart is home to five of the eleven state museums in <a href="/wiki/Baden-W%C3%BCrttemberg" title="Baden-Württemberg">Baden-Württemberg</a>. The foremost of these is the <a href="/wiki/Staatsgalerie_Stuttgart" title="Staatsgalerie Stuttgart">Old State Gallery</a> (opened in 1843, extended in 1984) which holds art dating from the 14th to 19th century including works by <a href="/wiki/Peter_Paul_Rubens" title="Peter Paul Rubens">Rubens</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rembrandt" title="Rembrandt">Rembrandt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Claude_Monet" title="Claude Monet">Monet</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pierre-Auguste_Renoir" title="Pierre-Auguste Renoir">Renoir</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paul_C%C3%A9zanne" title="Paul Cézanne">Cézanne</a> and <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Beuys" title="Joseph Beuys">Beuys</a>. Next door to the Old State Gallery is the <a href="/wiki/Neue_Staatsgalerie" title="Neue Staatsgalerie">New State Gallery</a> (1980) with its controversial modern architecture. Among others, this gallery houses works from <a href="/wiki/Max_Beckmann" title="Max Beckmann">Max Beckmann</a>, <a href="/wiki/Salvador_Dal%C3%AD" title="Salvador Dalí">Dalí</a>, <a href="/wiki/Henri_Matisse" title="Henri Matisse">Matisse</a>, <a href="/wiki/Joan_Mir%C3%B3" title="Joan Miró">Miró</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pablo_Picasso" title="Pablo Picasso">Picasso</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paul_Klee" title="Paul Klee">Klee</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marc_Chagall" title="Marc Chagall">Chagall</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wassily_Kandinsky" title="Wassily Kandinsky">Kandinsky</a>.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Old_Castle_(Stuttgart)" title="Old Castle (Stuttgart)">Old Castle</a> is also home to the <a href="/wiki/Landesmuseum_W%C3%BCrttemberg" title="Landesmuseum Württemberg">State Museum of Württemberg</a> which was founded in 1862 by <a href="/wiki/William_I_of_W%C3%BCrttemberg" title="William I of Württemberg">William I of Württemberg</a>. The museum traces the rich <a href="/wiki/History_of_W%C3%BCrttemberg" class="mw-redirect" title="History of Württemberg">history of Württemberg</a> with many artifacts from the its dukes, counts and kings, as well as earlier remnants dating back to the <a href="/wiki/Stone_Age" title="Stone Age">stone age</a>. On the Karlsplatz side of the Old Castle is a museum dedicated to the memory of <a href="/wiki/Claus_Schenk_Graf_von_Stauffenberg" class="mw-redirect" title="Claus Schenk Graf von Stauffenberg">Claus Schenk Graf von Stauffenberg</a>, former resident of Stuttgart who attempted to assassinate <a href="/wiki/Adolf_Hitler" title="Adolf Hitler">Adolf Hitler</a> on <a href="/wiki/20_July_plot" title="20 July plot">20 July 1944</a>.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mercedes-Benz_Museum_201312_08_blue_hour.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Mercedes-Benz_Museum_201312_08_blue_hour.jpg/220px-Mercedes-Benz_Museum_201312_08_blue_hour.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Mercedes-Benz_Museum_201312_08_blue_hour.jpg/330px-Mercedes-Benz_Museum_201312_08_blue_hour.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Mercedes-Benz_Museum_201312_08_blue_hour.jpg/440px-Mercedes-Benz_Museum_201312_08_blue_hour.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2600" data-file-height="1727" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mercedes-Benz_Museum_201312_08_blue_hour.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Mercedes-Benz_Museum" title="Mercedes-Benz Museum">Mercedes-Benz Museum</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Porsche-Museum_Main_Entrance.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Porsche-Museum_Main_Entrance.JPG/220px-Porsche-Museum_Main_Entrance.JPG" width="220" height="153" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Porsche-Museum_Main_Entrance.JPG/330px-Porsche-Museum_Main_Entrance.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Porsche-Museum_Main_Entrance.JPG/440px-Porsche-Museum_Main_Entrance.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2268" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Porsche-Museum_Main_Entrance.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Porsche_Museum,_Stuttgart" title="Porsche Museum, Stuttgart">Porsche Museum</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Other leading museums in Stuttgart include:</p>
<ul>
<li>The History Museum (<i>Haus der Geschichte</i>, 1987), examining local history, finds, the conflict between modern society and its cultural history</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/State_Museum_of_Natural_History_Stuttgart" title="State Museum of Natural History Stuttgart">State Museum of Natural History Stuttgart</a> (SMNS) in <a href="/wiki/Rosensteinpark" class="mw-redirect" title="Rosensteinpark">Park Rosenstein</a> housed in <a href="/wiki/Rosenstein_Castle" class="mw-redirect" title="Rosenstein Castle">Castle Rosenstein</a> (with an emphasis on biology and natural history) and Löwentor Museum (<a href="/wiki/Paleontology" title="Paleontology">paleontology</a> and geology, home of the <a href="/wiki/Steinheim_Skull" class="mw-redirect" title="Steinheim Skull">Steinheim Skull</a> and many unique fossils from the <a href="/wiki/Triassic" title="Triassic">triassic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jurassic" title="Jurassic">jurassic</a> and tertiary periods)</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Mercedes-Benz_Museum" title="Mercedes-Benz Museum">Mercedes-Benz Museum</a> (1936, moved in 2006), now the most visited museum in Stuttgart (440,000 visits per year).<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">[155]</a></sup> The museum traces the 125-year history of the automobile from the legendary silver arrow to the <a href="/wiki/Mercedes-Benz" title="Mercedes-Benz">Mercedes-Benz</a> brand of today</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Kunstmuseum_Stuttgart" title="Kunstmuseum Stuttgart">Stuttgart Art Museum</a> (<i>Kunstmuseum Stuttgart</i>, 2005), the number two museum in Stuttgart in terms of visitors with a strong leaning towards modern art (the foremost exhibition of <a href="/wiki/Otto_Dix" title="Otto Dix">Otto Dix</a> works. The museum stands on the corner of <a href="/wiki/Schlossplatz,_Stuttgart" class="mw-redirect" title="Schlossplatz, Stuttgart">Schlossplatz, Stuttgart</a> in a huge glass cube, in strong contrast to the surrounding traditional architecture.</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Porsche_Museum,_Stuttgart" title="Porsche Museum, Stuttgart">Porsche Museum</a> (1976, reopened in 2008 on new premises).</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hegel_House" title="Hegel House">Hegel House</a> (<i>Hegelhaus</i>), birthplace of the philosopher <a href="/wiki/Georg_Wilhelm_Friedrich_Hegel" title="Georg Wilhelm Friedrich Hegel">Georg Wilhelm Friedrich Hegel</a> which documents his life works</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Linden_Museum" title="Linden Museum">Linden Museum</a>, established in 1911, a leading international <a href="/wiki/Ethnology" title="Ethnology">ethnological</a> museum<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">[156]</a></sup></li>
<li>Stuttgart Tram Museum (<i>Straßenbahnwelt Stuttgart</i>) in Bad Cannstatt, a display of historical vehicles dating back to 1868</li>
<li>Theodor Heuss House (<i><a href="/wiki/Theodor_Heuss" title="Theodor Heuss">Theodor-Heuss</a>-Haus</i>, 2002) in <a href="/wiki/Killesbergpark" title="Killesbergpark">Killesbergpark</a>, a tribute to the life and times of the former German president</li>
<li>The North Station Memorial (<i>Gedenkstätte am Nordbahnhof Stuttgart)</i> in memory of the 2000 or so Jewish <a href="/wiki/The_Holocaust" title="The Holocaust">holocaust</a> victims deported by the <a href="/wiki/Nazism" title="Nazism">Nazis</a> from the now disused North Station</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Churches">Churches</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stuttgart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Churches">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Stuttgart is the seat of a <a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">Protestant</a> bishop (Protestant State Church in Württemberg) and one of the two co-seats of the bishop of the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_Rottenburg-Stuttgart" title="Roman Catholic Diocese of Rottenburg-Stuttgart">Roman Catholic Diocese of Rottenburg-Stuttgart</a>. The Stuttgart-based <a href="/wiki/Pentecostalism" title="Pentecostalism">Pentecostal</a> <i>Gospel Forum</i> is the largest place of worship (<a href="/wiki/Megachurch" title="Megachurch">megachurch</a>) in Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">[157]</a></sup> It is also home to a large English speaking church, The International Baptist Church of Stuttgart.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">[158]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Libraries">Libraries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stuttgart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Libraries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:BibliothekMailaenderPlatzNachtaufnahme_2012-01.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/BibliothekMailaenderPlatzNachtaufnahme_2012-01.jpg/220px-BibliothekMailaenderPlatzNachtaufnahme_2012-01.jpg" width="220" height="151" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/BibliothekMailaenderPlatzNachtaufnahme_2012-01.jpg/330px-BibliothekMailaenderPlatzNachtaufnahme_2012-01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/BibliothekMailaenderPlatzNachtaufnahme_2012-01.jpg/440px-BibliothekMailaenderPlatzNachtaufnahme_2012-01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4130" data-file-height="2832" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:BibliothekMailaenderPlatzNachtaufnahme_2012-01.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
City Library</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Wuerttembergische_landesbibliothek_2005_05a.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Wuerttembergische_landesbibliothek_2005_05a.jpg/220px-Wuerttembergische_landesbibliothek_2005_05a.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Wuerttembergische_landesbibliothek_2005_05a.jpg/330px-Wuerttembergische_landesbibliothek_2005_05a.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Wuerttembergische_landesbibliothek_2005_05a.jpg/440px-Wuerttembergische_landesbibliothek_2005_05a.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2264" data-file-height="1501" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Wuerttembergische_landesbibliothek_2005_05a.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/W%C3%BCrttembergische_Landesbibliothek" title="Württembergische Landesbibliothek">State Library of Wurttemberg</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hstas.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Hstas.jpg/220px-Hstas.jpg" width="220" height="93" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Hstas.jpg/330px-Hstas.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Hstas.jpg/440px-Hstas.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2893" data-file-height="1228" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hstas.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Central State Archive</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/W%C3%BCrttembergische_Landesbibliothek" title="Württembergische Landesbibliothek">State Library of Wurttemberg</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Badische_Landesbibliothek" class="mw-redirect" title="Badische Landesbibliothek">Badische Landesbibliothek</a> (BLB) in <a href="/wiki/Karlsruhe" title="Karlsruhe">Karlsruhe</a> regional library for Baden-Württemberg. The WLB is specifically responsible for the administrative regions of Stuttgart and Tübingen. Especially devoted to the National Library of acquiring, cataloging, archiving and provision of literature about Württemberg, called <i>Württembergica</i>. Together with the BLB it also has the legal deposit for Baden-Württemberg (since 1964, previously only Wuerttemberg), making it an archive library.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Stuttgart_University" class="mw-redirect" title="Stuttgart University">Stuttgart University</a> Library (UBS) is a central institution of the University of Stuttgart . It forms the center of the library system of the University, ensuring the supply of research, teaching and studies with literature and other information resources. It stands next to the members of the University and citizens of the city are available. Together with other research libraries and documentation centers in the Stuttgart area – such as the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Hohenheim" title="University of Hohenheim">University of Hohenheim</a> Library – it forms the UBS Library Information System of the Stuttgart Region (BISS).</p>
<p>The Central State Archive Stuttgart is the archive in charge of the Ministries of the State of Baden-Württemberg. Since 1965, it is located right next to the WLB and belongs since 2005 as a department of the Landesarchiv Baden-Württemberg in. It includes the stocks of the county and the duchy Württemberg until 1806, the Württemberg central authorities of the 19th and 20th century and the early 19th century as a result of media coverage of fallen Württemberg gentlemen and imperial cities in South Württemberg.</p>
<p>The Stadtarchiv Stuttgart is the archive in charge of the provincial capital Stuttgart. The archived material is in principle open to the public and can be consulted in the reading room in Bellingweg 21 in Bad Cannstatt.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Landeskirche" title="Landeskirche">Landeskirchliche</a> Archives preserve the stocks of the Württemberg church leaders and of other ecclesial bodies and institutions: the ducal and royal Württemberg consistory, the Evangelical Supreme Ecclesiastical Council, deanery and parish archives, educational institutions, the works and associations as well as estates and collections. It also has the microfilms of all church books (especially baptism, marriage, and family Death's Register) in the area of the <a href="/wiki/Evangelical-Lutheran_Church_in_W%C3%BCrttemberg" title="Evangelical-Lutheran Church in Württemberg">Evangelical-Lutheran Church in Württemberg</a>.</p>
<p>The "Archive instigator" is dedicated to the dead of the city. Since 2005, the instigators are working on a memoir about "The dead town". So far, about 5,000 names of victims of the regime of <a href="/wiki/Nazism" title="Nazism">National Socialism</a> have been acquired.</p>
<p>There are two large tours that are available to visitors to Stuttgart. The first is the Hop-on Hop-off bus tour (also called the CityTour Stuttgart), lasting from 10 AM to 4 PM that takes visitors around the city.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChristiani2015310_167-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChristiani2015310-167">[159]</a></sup> The other is the Neckar-Käpt'n, only available from May to October, which cruises on the Neckar river from its dock at <a href="/wiki/Wilhelma" title="Wilhelma">Wilhelma</a> in <a href="/wiki/Bad_Cannstatt" title="Bad Cannstatt">Bad Cannstatt</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChristiani2015311_160-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChristiani2015311-160">[152]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stuttgart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The population of Stuttgart declined steadily between 1960 (637,539) and 2000 (586,978). Then low levels of unemployment and attractive secondary education opportunities led to renewed population growth, fuelled especially by young adults from the <a href="/wiki/New_states_of_Germany" title="New states of Germany">former East Germany</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">[160]</a></sup> For the first time in decades, in 2006 there were also more births in the city than deaths. In April 2008 there were 590,720 inhabitants in the city.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">[161]</a></sup></p>
