<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Immigrants">Immigrants</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stuttgart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Immigrants">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Update" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div style="width:52px"><img alt="Ambox current red.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/42px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png" width="42" height="34" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/63px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/84px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="360" data-file-height="290" /></div>
</td>
<td class="mbox-text">
<div class="mbox-text-span">This section needs to be <b>updated</b>. <span class="hide-when-compact">Please update this article to reflect recent events or newly available information.</span> <small><i>(June 2017)</i></small></div>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>More than half of the population today is not of <a href="/wiki/Swabia" title="Swabia">Swabian</a> background, as many non-Swabian Germans have moved here due to the employment situation, which is far better than in most areas of Germany. Since the 1960s, many foreigners have also immigrated to Stuttgart to work here (as part of the "<a href="/wiki/Gastarbeiter" title="Gastarbeiter">Gastarbeiter</a>" program); another wave of immigrants came as refugees from the <a href="/wiki/Wars_in_Yugoslavia" class="mw-redirect" title="Wars in Yugoslavia">Wars in Yugoslavia</a> in the 1990s. Thus, 40% of the city's population is of foreign background. In 2000, 22.8% of the population did not hold <a href="/wiki/German_nationality_law" title="German nationality law">German citizenship</a>, in 2006 this had reduced to 21.7%. The largest groups of foreign nationals were <a href="/wiki/Turkish_people" title="Turkish people">Turks</a> (22,025), <a href="/wiki/Greeks" title="Greeks">Greeks</a> (14,341), <a href="/wiki/Italian_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Italian people">Italians</a> (13,978), <a href="/wiki/Croats" title="Croats">Croats</a> (12,985), <a href="/wiki/Serbs" title="Serbs">Serbs</a> (11,547) followed by immigrants from Romania, Bosnia and Herzegovina, Portugal, Poland, France, and Austria. 39% of foreign nationals come from the European Union (mostly Italy, Greece, and Poland).</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stuttgart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The religious landscape in Stuttgart changed in 1534 as a direct result of the <a href="/wiki/Protestant_Reformation" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestant Reformation">Reformation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchlaichHeckelHeun199728_171-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchlaichHeckelHeun199728-171">[163]</a></sup> Since this time <a href="/wiki/W%C3%BCrttemberg" title="Württemberg">Württemberg</a> has been predominantly <a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">Protestant</a>. However, since 1975 the number of Protestants in Stuttgart has dropped from around 300,000 to 200,000. In 2014, 26.2% of inhabitants were <a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">Protestant</a> and 24.0% were Roman Catholic. 49.8% of the population fell into other categories: Muslims, Jews and those who either followed no religion or one not accounted for in official statistics.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">[164]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Unemployment">Unemployment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stuttgart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Unemployment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Unemployment in the <a href="/wiki/Stuttgart_Region" title="Stuttgart Region">Stuttgart Region</a> is above the average of <a href="/wiki/Baden-W%C3%BCrttemberg" title="Baden-Württemberg">Baden-Württemberg</a>, but very low compared to other metropolitan areas in Germany. In November 2008, before the annual winter rise, unemployment in the Stuttgart Region stood at 3.8%, 0.1% lower than the rate for <a href="/wiki/Baden-W%C3%BCrttemberg" title="Baden-Württemberg">Baden-Württemberg</a>, in February 2009 it was 4.7%. Unemployment in the actual city of Stuttgart during the same periods stood at 5.2% and 6.0% (8 Nov and 9 Feb respectively). By comparison: unemployment for the whole of Germany stood at 7.1% (8 Nov) and 8.5% (9 Feb).<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">[165]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">[166]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Crime_rates">Crime rates</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stuttgart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Crime rates">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Stuttgart ranks as one of the safest cities in Germany. In 2003, 8535 crimes were committed in Stuttgart for every 100,000 inhabitants (versus the average for all German cities of 12,751).<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">[167]</a></sup> Figures for 2006 indicate that Stuttgart ranked second behind <a href="/wiki/Munich" title="Munich">Munich</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">[168]</a></sup> 60% of Stuttgart crimes were solved in 2003, ranking second behind <a href="/wiki/Nuremberg" title="Nuremberg">Nuremberg</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stuttgart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Stuttgart_Rathaus01.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Stuttgart_Rathaus01.JPG/170px-Stuttgart_Rathaus01.JPG" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Stuttgart_Rathaus01.JPG/255px-Stuttgart_Rathaus01.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Stuttgart_Rathaus01.JPG/340px-Stuttgart_Rathaus01.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2136" data-file-height="2848" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Stuttgart_Rathaus01.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Stuttgart Town Hall (Rathaus)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Stuttgart's current <a href="/wiki/Burgomaster" title="Burgomaster">Bürgermeister</a> (mayor) is <a href="/wiki/Fritz_Kuhn" title="Fritz Kuhn">Fritz Kuhn</a> of the centre-left <a href="/wiki/Alliance_%2790/The_Greens" class="mw-redirect" title="Alliance '90/The Greens">Alliance '90/The Greens</a> party (German Green party).</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="City_government_past_and_present">City government past and present</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stuttgart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: City government past and present">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>When Stuttgart was run as a (or within) the <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_W%C3%BCrttemberg" title="Duchy of Württemberg">Duchy of Württemberg</a>, it was governed by a type of protectorate called a <a href="/wiki/Vogt" title="Vogt">Vogt</a> appointed by the <a href="/wiki/Duke" title="Duke">Duke</a>. After 1811 this role was fulfilled by a City Director or 'Stadtdirektor'. After 1819 the community elected its own community mayor or 'Schultheiß'. Since 1930 the title of Oberbürgermeister (the nearest equivalent of which would be an executive form of <a href="/wiki/Lord_Mayor" class="mw-redirect" title="Lord Mayor">Lord Mayor</a> in English) has applied to Stuttgart and all other Württemberg towns of more than 20,000 inhabitants.</p>
<p>At the end of the Second World War, French administrators appointed the independent politician <a href="/wiki/Arnulf_Klett" title="Arnulf Klett">Arnulf Klett</a> as <a href="/wiki/Burgomaster" title="Burgomaster">Burgomaster</a>, a role he fulfilled without interruption until his death in 1974. Since this time Stuttgart has mainly been governed by the <a href="/wiki/Christian_Democratic_Union_(Germany)" class="mw-redirect" title="Christian Democratic Union (Germany)">CDU</a>. One former mayor was <a href="/wiki/Manfred_Rommel" title="Manfred Rommel">Manfred Rommel</a> (son of perhaps the most famous German <a href="/wiki/Field_Marshal" class="mw-redirect" title="Field Marshal">field marshal</a> of World War II, <a href="/wiki/Erwin_Rommel" title="Erwin Rommel">Erwin Rommel</a>).</p>
<p>As the capital of <a href="/wiki/Baden-W%C3%BCrttemberg" title="Baden-Württemberg">Baden-Württemberg</a>, Stuttgart is an important political centre in Germany and the seat of the State Parliament, or <a href="/wiki/Landtag" title="Landtag">Landtag</a> as well as all <a href="/wiki/Baden-W%C3%BCrttemberg" title="Baden-Württemberg">Baden-Württemberg</a> state departments.</p>
<p>In June 2009, for the first time the <a href="/wiki/Green_party" title="Green party">Greens</a> gained the most seats in a German city with more than 500,000 inhabitants, effectively changing the balance of power in the city council. For the first time since 1972 the <a href="/wiki/Christian_Democratic_Union_(Germany)" class="mw-redirect" title="Christian Democratic Union (Germany)">CDU</a> no longer held the most seats, toppling its absolute majority shared with the Independent Party and the <a href="/wiki/Free_Democratic_Party_(Germany)" title="Free Democratic Party (Germany)">FDP</a>. According to the German newspaper <a href="/wiki/Die_Welt" title="Die Welt">Die Welt</a>, the main reason for the Greens' victory was disgruntlement with the controversial <a href="/wiki/Stuttgart_21" title="Stuttgart 21">Stuttgart 21</a> rail project.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">[169]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Municipalities">Municipalities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stuttgart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Municipalities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The city of Stuttgart is administratively divided into 23 <a href="/wiki/Stadtbezirk" title="Stadtbezirk">city districts</a><sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">[170]</a></sup> – five "Inner" districts and 18 "Outer" districts. Each district has a Council headed by a District Director. From there, the districts are broken down into <a href="/wiki/Quarter_(urban_subdivision)" title="Quarter (urban subdivision)">Quarters</a>. Since the changes in city statutes 1 July 2007 and 1 January 2009, the total number of quarters rose to 152.{<a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=VH5zW6GOAIoC&amp;pg=PA132&amp;lpg=PA132&amp;dq=stuttgart+city+districts&amp;source=bl&amp;ots=jfT5UrriY4&amp;sig=-Gv_7hI6n_zPdeVRlcd4s2F2lEs&amp;hl=en&amp;sa=X&amp;ved=0ahUKEwif9ZWE7KfWAhVklFQKHU6eBSs4ChDoAQg0MAM#v=onepage&amp;q=stuttgart%20city%20districts&amp;f=false{}}">https://books.google.com/books?id=VH5zW6GOAIoC&amp;pg=PA132&amp;lpg=PA132&amp;dq=stuttgart+city+districts&amp;source=bl&amp;ots=jfT5UrriY4&amp;sig=-Gv_7hI6n_zPdeVRlcd4s2F2lEs&amp;hl=en&amp;sa=X&amp;ved=0ahUKEwif9ZWE7KfWAhVklFQKHU6eBSs4ChDoAQg0MAM#v=onepage&amp;q=stuttgart%20city%20districts&amp;f=false{}}</a></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stuttgart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The Stuttgart area is known for its high-tech industry. Some of its most prominent companies include <a href="/wiki/Daimler_AG" title="Daimler AG">Daimler AG</a>, <a href="/wiki/Porsche" title="Porsche">Porsche</a>, <a href="/wiki/Robert_Bosch_GmbH" title="Robert Bosch GmbH">Bosch</a>, <a href="/wiki/Celesio" title="Celesio">Celesio</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hewlett-Packard" title="Hewlett-Packard">Hewlett-Packard</a>, <a href="/wiki/IBM" title="IBM">IBM</a>, Sika – all of whom have their world or European headquarters here.</p>
<p>Stuttgart is home to Germany's ninth biggest exhibition center, <a href="/wiki/Stuttgart_Trade_Fair" title="Stuttgart Trade Fair">Stuttgart Trade Fair</a> which lies on the city outskirts next to <a href="/wiki/Stuttgart_Airport" title="Stuttgart Airport">Stuttgart Airport</a>. Hundreds of <a href="/wiki/Small_and_medium_enterprises" class="mw-redirect" title="Small and medium enterprises">SMEs</a> are still based in Stuttgart (often termed <i><a href="/wiki/Mittelstand" title="Mittelstand">Mittelstand</a></i>), many still in family ownership with strong ties to the automotive, electronics, engineering and high-tech industry.</p>
<p>Stuttgart has the highest general standard of prosperity of any city in Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">[172]</a></sup> Its nominal GDP per capita is €57,100 and GDP purchasing power parity (PPP) per capita is €55,400. Total GDP of Stuttgart is €33.9&#160;billion, of which service sector contributes around 65.3%, industry 34.5%, and agriculture 0.2%.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2009)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_cradle_of_the_automobile">The cradle of the automobile</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stuttgart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: The cradle of the automobile">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The automobile and motorcycle were purported to have been invented in Stuttgart (by <a href="/wiki/Karl_Benz" title="Karl Benz">Karl Benz</a> and subsequently industrialized in 1887 by <a href="/wiki/Gottlieb_Daimler" title="Gottlieb Daimler">Gottlieb Daimler</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wilhelm_Maybach" title="Wilhelm Maybach">Wilhelm Maybach</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Daimler-Motoren-Gesellschaft" title="Daimler-Motoren-Gesellschaft">Daimler Motoren Gesellschaft</a>). As a result, it is considered to be the starting point of the worldwide automotive industry and is sometimes referred to as the 'cradle of the automobile'.<sup id="cite_ref-Amondson_22-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Amondson-22">[20]</a></sup> Today, <a href="/wiki/Mercedes-Benz" title="Mercedes-Benz">Mercedes-Benz</a> and <a href="/wiki/Porsche" title="Porsche">Porsche</a> both have their headquarters in Stuttgart, as well as automotive parts giants <a href="/wiki/Robert_Bosch_GmbH" title="Robert Bosch GmbH">Bosch</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mahle_GmbH" title="Mahle GmbH">Mahle</a>. A number of auto-enthusiast magazines are published in Stuttgart.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT_181-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT-181">[173]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Science_and_research_and_development">Science and research and development</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stuttgart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Science and research and development">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The region currently has Germany's highest density of scientific, academic and research organisations. No other region in Germany registers so many patents and designs as Stuttgart.<sup id="cite_ref-Where_Business_Meets_the_Future_85-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Where_Business_Meets_the_Future-85">[81]</a></sup> Almost 45% of <a href="/wiki/Baden-W%C3%BCrttemberg" title="Baden-Württemberg">Baden-Württemberg</a> scientists involved in R&amp;D are based directly in the Swabian capital. More than 11% of all German R&amp;D costs are invested in the Stuttgart Region (approximately 4.3&#160;billion euros per year). In addition to several universities and colleges (e.g. <a href="/wiki/University_of_Stuttgart" title="University of Stuttgart">University of Stuttgart</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Hohenheim" title="University of Hohenheim">University of Hohenheim</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stuttgart_Institute_of_Management_and_Technology" title="Stuttgart Institute of Management and Technology">Stuttgart Institute of Management and Technology</a><sup id="cite_ref-EBStutt_31-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EBStutt-31">[29]</a></sup> and several Stuttgart <a href="/wiki/University_of_Applied_Sciences_Stuttgart" class="mw-redirect" title="University of Applied Sciences Stuttgart">Universities of Applied Sciences</a>), the area is home to six <a href="/wiki/Fraunhofer_Society" title="Fraunhofer Society">Fraunhofer</a> institutes, four institutes of collaborative industrial research at local universities, two <a href="/wiki/Max_Planck_Society" title="Max Planck Society">Max-Planck institutes</a> and a major establishment of the <a href="/wiki/German_Aerospace_Center" title="German Aerospace Center">German Aerospace Centre (DLR)</a>.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Koenigsbau_Stuttgart_20060901.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Koenigsbau_Stuttgart_20060901.jpg/220px-Koenigsbau_Stuttgart_20060901.jpg" width="220" height="90" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Koenigsbau_Stuttgart_20060901.jpg/330px-Koenigsbau_Stuttgart_20060901.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Koenigsbau_Stuttgart_20060901.jpg/440px-Koenigsbau_Stuttgart_20060901.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2904" data-file-height="1193" /></a>

</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Financial_services">Financial services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stuttgart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Financial services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Stuttgart Stock Exchange is the second largest in Germany (after <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Stock_Exchange" title="Frankfurt Stock Exchange">Frankfurt</a>). Many leading companies in the financial services sector are headquartered in Stuttgart with around 100 credit institutes in total (e.g. <a href="/wiki/Landesbank_Baden-W%C3%BCrttemberg" title="Landesbank Baden-Württemberg">LBBW Bank</a>, Wüstenrot &amp; Württembergische, <a href="/wiki/Allianz" title="Allianz">Allianz</a> Life Assurance).</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kriegsberg.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Kriegsberg.jpg/220px-Kriegsberg.jpg" width="220" height="196" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Kriegsberg.jpg/330px-Kriegsberg.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Kriegsberg.jpg/440px-Kriegsberg.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1728" data-file-height="1536" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kriegsberg.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i>Kriegsberg</i> vineyard in the city center</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="A_history_of_wine_and_beer">A history of wine and beer</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stuttgart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: A history of wine and beer">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Stuttgart is the only city in Germany where wine grapes are grown within the urban area, mainly in the districts of Rotenberg, Uhlbach and Untertürkheim.</p>
<p>Wine-growing in the area dates back to 1108 when, according to State archives, <a href="/wiki/Blaubeuren_Abbey" title="Blaubeuren Abbey">Blaubeuren Abbey</a> was given vineyards in Stuttgart as a gift from 'Monk Ulrich'. In the 17th century the city was the third largest German wine-growing community in the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">Holy Roman Empire</a>. Wine remained Stuttgart's leading source of income well into the 19th century.</p>
<p>Stuttgart is still one of Germany's largest wine-growing cities with more than 400 hectares of vine area, thanks in main to its location at the center of Germany's fourth largest wine region, the <a href="/wiki/W%C3%BCrttemberg_(wine_region)" title="Württemberg (wine region)">Württemberg wine growing area</a> which covers 11,522 hectares (28,470 acres) and is one of only 13 official areas captured under German <a href="/wiki/Wine_law" title="Wine law">Wine law</a>. The continuing importance of wine to the local economy is marked every year at the annual wine festival ('Weindorf').</p>
<p>Stuttgart also has several famous breweries such as <a href="/wiki/Stuttgarter_Hofbr%C3%A4u" title="Stuttgarter Hofbräu">Stuttgarter Hofbräu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dinkelacker" title="Dinkelacker">Dinkelacker</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Schwaben_Br%C3%A4u" title="Schwaben Bräu">Schwaben Bräu</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education_and_research">Education and research</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stuttgart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Education and research">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Stuttgart_HochschuleFuerMusikUndDarstellendeKunst.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Stuttgart_HochschuleFuerMusikUndDarstellendeKunst.jpg/220px-Stuttgart_HochschuleFuerMusikUndDarstellendeKunst.jpg" width="220" height="172" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Stuttgart_HochschuleFuerMusikUndDarstellendeKunst.jpg/330px-Stuttgart_HochschuleFuerMusikUndDarstellendeKunst.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Stuttgart_HochschuleFuerMusikUndDarstellendeKunst.jpg/440px-Stuttgart_HochschuleFuerMusikUndDarstellendeKunst.jpg 2x" data-file-width="764" data-file-height="596" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Stuttgart_HochschuleFuerMusikUndDarstellendeKunst.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The new building of the State University of Music and Performing Arts, designed by <a href="/wiki/James_Stirling_(architect)" title="James Stirling (architect)">James Stirling</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Stuttgart and its region have been home to some significant figures of German thought and literature, the most important ones being <a href="/wiki/Georg_Wilhelm_Friedrich_Hegel" title="Georg Wilhelm Friedrich Hegel">Georg Wilhelm Friedrich Hegel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Friedrich_Schiller" title="Friedrich Schiller">Friedrich Schiller</a> and <a href="/wiki/Friedrich_H%C3%B6lderlin" title="Friedrich Hölderlin">Friedrich Hölderlin</a>.</p>
<p>The city, in its engineering tradition as the cradle of the automobile, has also always been a fruitful place of research and innovation. Stuttgart has Germany's second-highest number of institutions (six) of applied research of the <a href="/wiki/Fraunhofer_Society" title="Fraunhofer Society">Fraunhofer Society</a> (after <a href="/wiki/Dresden" title="Dresden">Dresden</a>).</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tertiary_education">Tertiary education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stuttgart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Tertiary education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The city is not considered a traditional university city, but nevertheless has a variety of institutions of higher education. The most significant of them are:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Stuttgart" title="University of Stuttgart">University of Stuttgart</a>, it is the fourth biggest university in Baden-Württemberg after <a href="/wiki/University_of_Heidelberg" class="mw-redirect" title="University of Heidelberg">Heidelberg</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_T%C3%BCbingen" title="University of Tübingen">Tübingen</a> and <a href="/wiki/University_of_Freiburg" title="University of Freiburg">Freiburg</a>. Founded in 1829, it was a <i>Technische Hochschule</i> ("Technical University") until 1967, when it was renamed to "university". Its campus for social sciences and architecture is located in the city centre, near the <a href="/wiki/Stuttgart_Hauptbahnhof" title="Stuttgart Hauptbahnhof">main train station</a>, while the natural science campus is in the southwestern city district of Vaihingen. Historically, it has been especially renowned for its faculty of architecture (<i>Stuttgarter Schule</i>). Today, its main focus is on engineering and other technical subjects.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Hohenheim" title="University of Hohenheim">University of Hohenheim</a>, founded in 1818 as an academy for <a href="/wiki/Agricultural_science" title="Agricultural science">agricultural science</a> and <a href="/wiki/Forestry" title="Forestry">forestry</a>. While these subjects are still taught there today, its other focus today is on business administration. It is located in Hohenheim quarter of the southern city district of Plieningen.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/State_University_of_Music_and_Performing_Arts_Stuttgart" title="State University of Music and Performing Arts Stuttgart">State University of Music and Performing Arts Stuttgart</a>, founded in 1857, located in the city center, next to the <a href="/wiki/Neue_Staatsgalerie" title="Neue Staatsgalerie">Neue Staatsgalerie</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/State_Academy_of_Fine_Arts_in_Stuttgart" title="State Academy of Fine Arts in Stuttgart">State Academy of Fine Arts in Stuttgart</a>, one of the biggest art colleges in Germany, founded in 1761, located in the Killesberg quarter of the northern city district Stuttgart-Nord.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hochschule_der_Medien" class="mw-redirect" title="Hochschule der Medien">Stuttgart Media University</a> (Hochschule der Medien Stuttgart), founded in 2001 as a university of applied sciences, a merger of the former <i>College of Printing and Publishing</i> and the <i>College of Librarianship</i>, located in Vaihingen.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Applied_Sciences_Stuttgart" class="mw-redirect" title="University of Applied Sciences Stuttgart">Stuttgart Technology University of Applied Sciences (Hochschule für Technik Stuttgart)</a>, founded in 1832 as a college for craftsmanship, university of applied sciences since 1971, located in the city center, near the University of Stuttgart's city-center campus.</li>
<li>University of Cooperative Education Baden-Württemberg, founded in 1974, with a focus on practical experience, subjects are business, technology and social work.</li>
</ul>
<p>Historically, an elite <a href="/wiki/Military_academy" title="Military academy">military academy</a> existed in Stuttgart in the late 18th century (1770–1794), the <a href="/wiki/Hohe_Karlsschule" class="mw-redirect" title="Hohe Karlsschule">Hohe Karlsschule</a>, at Solitude Castle. Friedrich Schiller and the city's most famous <a href="/wiki/Classicism" title="Classicism">Classicist architect</a>, Nikolaus Friedrich von Thouret, were among its many esteemed alumni.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Primary_and_secondary_education">Primary and secondary education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stuttgart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Primary and secondary education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The first <a href="/wiki/Waldorf_School" class="mw-redirect" title="Waldorf School">Waldorf School</a> (also known as Rudolf Steiner School) was founded here in 1919 by the director of the <a href="/wiki/Waldorf-Astoria-Zigarettenfabrik" title="Waldorf-Astoria-Zigarettenfabrik">Waldorf Astoria tobacco factory</a>, <a href="/wiki/Emil_Molt" title="Emil Molt">Emil Molt</a>, and Austrian social thinker <a href="/wiki/Rudolf_Steiner" title="Rudolf Steiner">Rudolf Steiner</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Comprehensive_school" title="Comprehensive school">comprehensive school</a> following Steiner's educational principles of <a href="/wiki/Anthroposophy" title="Anthroposophy">anthroposophy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Humanism" title="Humanism">humanistic</a> ideals. Today, four of these schools are located in Stuttgart.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="International_School">International School</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stuttgart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: International School">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Since 1985 Stuttgart is home to the International School of Stuttgart,<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">[174]</a></sup> one of less than 100 schools worldwide that offer all three <a href="/wiki/International_Baccalaureate" title="International Baccalaureate">International Baccalaureate</a> programs- the IB Primary Years (Early Learning to Grade 5), IB Middle Years (Grade 6 to 10), IB Diploma (grades 11–12).<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">[175]</a></sup> The International School of Stuttgart is accredited by both the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Council_of_International_Schools&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Council of International Schools (page does not exist)">Council of International Schools</a> and the <a href="/wiki/New_England_Association_of_Schools_and_Colleges" title="New England Association of Schools and Colleges">New England Association of Schools and Colleges</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">[176]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Media_and_publishing">Media and publishing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stuttgart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Media and publishing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>One of the headquarters of the public <a href="/wiki/S%C3%BCdwestrundfunk" title="Südwestrundfunk">Südwestrundfunk</a> (SWR; <i>Southwest Broadcasting</i>) channels (several radio and one TV channel; regional focus on the southwestern German States of Baden-Württemberg and <a href="/wiki/Rhineland-Palatinate" title="Rhineland-Palatinate">Rhineland-Palatinate</a>) is located in Stuttgart (the other ones being <a href="/wiki/Baden-Baden" title="Baden-Baden">Baden-Baden</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mainz" title="Mainz">Mainz</a>). It also has a <i>Landesmedienzentrum</i>, a State media center.</p>
<p>Furthermore, the city is a significant centre of publishing and specialist printing, with renowned houses such as <a href="/wiki/Verlagsgruppe_Georg_von_Holtzbrinck" class="mw-redirect" title="Verlagsgruppe Georg von Holtzbrinck">Georg von Holtzbrinck Publishing Group</a>, <a href="https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ernst_Klett_Verlag" class="extiw" title="de:Ernst Klett Verlag">Ernst Klett Verlag</a> (schoolbooks), Kohlhammer Verlag, Metzler Verlag and <a href="/wiki/Motor_Presse" class="mw-redirect" title="Motor Presse">Motor Presse</a> having their head offices there. The <a href="/wiki/Reclam" title="Reclam">Reclam</a> Verlag is located in nearby <a href="/wiki/Ditzingen" title="Ditzingen">Ditzingen</a>.</p>
<p>The newspapers <i><a href="/wiki/Stuttgarter_Zeitung" title="Stuttgarter Zeitung">Stuttgarter Zeitung</a></i> (StZ; regional, with significant supra-regional, national and international sections) and Stuttgarter Nachrichten (StN; regional) are published here as well as a number of smaller, local papers such as <i>Cannstatter Zeitung</i>.</p>
<p>As is the case wherever the US military is stationed, there is an <a href="/wiki/American_Forces_Network" title="American Forces Network">American Forces Network</a> (AFN) station. It transmits on FM on 102.3&#160;MHz from <a href="/wiki/Fernmeldeturm_Frauenkopf" class="mw-redirect" title="Fernmeldeturm Frauenkopf">Fernmeldeturm Frauenkopf</a> and on AM on 1143&#160;kHz from <a href="/wiki/Hirschlanden_transmitter" title="Hirschlanden transmitter">Hirschlanden transmitter</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stuttgart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Following the suit of other German cities such as Berlin, <a href="/wiki/Cologne" title="Cologne">Cologne</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hanover" title="Hanover">Hanover</a>, on 1 March 2008 a <a href="/wiki/Low_emission_zone" class="mw-redirect" title="Low emission zone">Low Emission Zone</a> (LEZ) came into effect in Stuttgart with the aim of improving air quality. This affects all vehicles entering the Stuttgart 'Environmental zone' (<i>Umweltzone</i>), including vehicles from abroad.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">[177]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">[178]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Local_transport">Local transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stuttgart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Local transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

</div>
</div>
<p>Stuttgart has a <a href="/wiki/Light_rail" title="Light rail">light rail</a> system known as the <a href="/wiki/Stuttgart_Stadtbahn" title="Stuttgart Stadtbahn">Stuttgart Stadtbahn</a>. In the city center and densely built-up areas, the Stadtbahn runs underground. Stations are signposted with a 'U' symbol, which stands for <i>Untergrundbahn</i> (underground rail). Until 2007, Stuttgart also operated regular trams. Stuttgart also has a large bus network. Stadtbahn lines and buses are operated by the <a href="/wiki/Stuttgarter_Stra%C3%9Fenbahnen_AG" class="mw-redirect" title="Stuttgarter Straßenbahnen AG">Stuttgarter Straßenbahnen AG</a> (SSB). The outlying suburbs of Stuttgart and nearby towns are served by a suburban railway system called the <a href="/wiki/Stuttgart_S-Bahn" title="Stuttgart S-Bahn">Stuttgart S-Bahn</a>, using tracks supplied by the national <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Bahn" title="Deutsche Bahn">Deutsche Bahn</a> AG (DBAG).</p>
<p>A peculiarity of Stuttgart is the <a href="/wiki/Stuttgart_Rack_Railway" title="Stuttgart Rack Railway"><i>Zahnradbahn</i></a>, a <a href="/wiki/Rack_railway" title="Rack railway">rack railway</a> that is powered by electricity and operates between Marienplatz in the southern inner-city district of the city and the district of Degerloch. It is the only urban rack railway in Germany. Stuttgart also has a <a href="/wiki/Standseilbahn_Stuttgart" title="Standseilbahn Stuttgart"><i>Standseilbahn</i></a>, a <a href="/wiki/Funicular" title="Funicular">funicular</a> railway that operates in the Heslach area and the forest cemetery (Waldfriedhof). In <a href="/wiki/Killesbergpark" title="Killesbergpark">Killesberg Park</a>, on a prominent hill overlooking the city, there is the <a href="/wiki/Killesberg_Railway" title="Killesberg Railway">miniature railway</a> run by diesel (and on weekends with steam).</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rail_links">Rail links</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stuttgart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Rail links">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:EDDS_-_001.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/EDDS_-_001.jpg/220px-EDDS_-_001.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/EDDS_-_001.jpg/330px-EDDS_-_001.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/EDDS_-_001.jpg/440px-EDDS_-_001.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="479" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:EDDS_-_001.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Stuttgart Airport</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Stuttgart_zahnradbahn1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Stuttgart_zahnradbahn1.jpg/220px-Stuttgart_zahnradbahn1.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Stuttgart_zahnradbahn1.jpg/330px-Stuttgart_zahnradbahn1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Stuttgart_zahnradbahn1.jpg/440px-Stuttgart_zahnradbahn1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Stuttgart_zahnradbahn1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Stuttgart rack railway</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Stuttgart is a hub in the <a href="/wiki/Intercity-Express" title="Intercity-Express">InterCityExpress</a> and <a href="/wiki/InterCity" title="InterCity">InterCity</a> networks of <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Bahn" title="Deutsche Bahn">Deutsche Bahn</a> AG (DBAG), with through services to most other major German cities. It also operates international services to <a href="/wiki/Strasbourg" title="Strasbourg">Strasbourg</a>, Vienna, <a href="/wiki/Z%C3%BCrich" title="Zürich">Zürich</a> and Paris (five times a day, journey time 3 hours 11 minutes).<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">[179]</a></sup></p>
<p>Long distance trains stop at <a href="/wiki/Stuttgart_Hauptbahnhof" title="Stuttgart Hauptbahnhof">Stuttgart Hauptbahnhof</a>, the city's main line terminus which is also used by regional DBAG <a href="/wiki/Regional-Express" title="Regional-Express">RegionalExpress</a> and <a href="/wiki/Regionalbahn" title="Regionalbahn">RegionalBahn</a> for services to stations in the Stuttgart metropolitan area. The local rail networks (see above) operate underneath the terminus.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Stuttgart also has its own rail freight centre with <a href="/wiki/Classification_yard" title="Classification yard">marshalling yards</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Container_terminal" title="Container terminal">container terminal</a> in the Obertürkheim area of Hedelfingen.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rail:_The_Stuttgart_21_project">Rail: The <i>Stuttgart 21</i> project</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stuttgart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Rail: The Stuttgart 21 project">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>After years of political debate and controversy, plans were approved in October 2007 to convert the existing above-ground <a href="/wiki/Stuttgart_Hauptbahnhof" title="Stuttgart Hauptbahnhof">main train station</a> to an underground through station. The <i><a href="/wiki/Stuttgart_21" title="Stuttgart 21">Stuttgart 21</a> project</i> will include the rebuilding of surface and underground lines connecting the station in Stuttgart's enclosed central valley with existing railway and underground lines. Building work started in 2010 with controversial modifications to the Hauptbahnhof and should be completed in 2020.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Air_transport">Air transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stuttgart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Air transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Stuttgart is served by <a href="/wiki/Stuttgart_Airport" title="Stuttgart Airport">Stuttgart Airport</a> (German: <span lang="de">Flughafen Stuttgart</span>, IATA airport code <i>STR</i>), an international airport approximately 13&#160;km (8&#160;mi) south of the city centre on land belonging mainly to neighboring towns. It takes 30 minutes to reach the airport from the city center using <a href="/wiki/S-Bahn" class="mw-redirect" title="S-Bahn">S-Bahn</a> lines S2 or S3. Stuttgart airport is Germany's only international airport with one runway. Despite protests and local initiatives, surveys are currently underway to assess the impact of a second runway.<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">[180]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Road_transport">Road transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stuttgart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Road transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Stuttgart is served by <a href="/wiki/Bundesautobahn_8" title="Bundesautobahn 8">Autobahn A8</a>, that runs east-west from <a href="/wiki/Karlsruhe" title="Karlsruhe">Karlsruhe</a> to <a href="/wiki/Munich" title="Munich">Munich</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Bundesautobahn_81" title="Bundesautobahn 81">Autobahn A81</a> that runs north-south from <a href="/wiki/W%C3%BCrzburg" title="Würzburg">Würzburg</a> to <a href="/wiki/Singen" title="Singen">Singen</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Bundesautobahn_831" title="Bundesautobahn 831">Autobahn A831</a> is a short spur entering the southern side of Stuttgart.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Stuttgart-hafen-2005.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Stuttgart-hafen-2005.jpg/220px-Stuttgart-hafen-2005.jpg" width="220" height="117" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Stuttgart-hafen-2005.jpg/330px-Stuttgart-hafen-2005.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Stuttgart-hafen-2005.jpg/440px-Stuttgart-hafen-2005.jpg 2x" data-file-width="607" data-file-height="322" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Stuttgart-hafen-2005.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Port on Neckar River in Stuttgart</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Besides these Autobahns, Stuttgart is served by a large number of expressways, many of which are built to <a href="/wiki/Bundesautobahn" class="mw-redirect" title="Bundesautobahn">Autobahn</a> standards, and were once intended to carry an A-number. Important expressways like B10, B14, <a href="/wiki/Bundesstra%C3%9Fe_27" title="Bundesstraße 27">B27</a> and B29 connect Stuttgart with its suburbs. Due to the hilly surroundings, there are many road tunnels in and around Stuttgart. There are also a number of road tunnels under intersections in the center of Stuttgart.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Waterways">Waterways</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stuttgart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Waterways">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Stuttgart has an inland port in Hedelfingen on the <a href="/wiki/Neckar" title="Neckar">Neckar</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stuttgart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Sport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Football">Football</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stuttgart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: Football">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Gottlieb-daimler-stadion.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Gottlieb-daimler-stadion.jpg/220px-Gottlieb-daimler-stadion.jpg" width="220" height="98" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Gottlieb-daimler-stadion.jpg/330px-Gottlieb-daimler-stadion.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Gottlieb-daimler-stadion.jpg/440px-Gottlieb-daimler-stadion.jpg 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="222" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Gottlieb-daimler-stadion.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/VfB_Stuttgart" title="VfB Stuttgart">VfB Stuttgart</a>'s home ground, the <a href="/wiki/Mercedes-Benz_Arena_(Stuttgart)" title="Mercedes-Benz Arena (Stuttgart)">Mercedes-Benz Arena</a> in Bad Cannstatt. In the background: the <a href="/wiki/Stuttgart_Spring_Festival" title="Stuttgart Spring Festival">Stuttgart Spring Festival</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>As in the rest of Germany, football is the most popular sport in Stuttgart which is home to 'The Reds' and 'The Blues'. 'The Reds', <a href="/wiki/VfB_Stuttgart" title="VfB Stuttgart">VfB Stuttgart</a>, are the most famous and popular local club. An established team currently playing in the German <a href="/wiki/2._Bundesliga" title="2. Bundesliga">2. Bundesliga</a>, VfB was founded in 1893 and has won five German titles since 1950, most recently in 1992 and 2007. VfB is based at the <a href="/wiki/Mercedes-Benz_Arena_(Stuttgart)" title="Mercedes-Benz Arena (Stuttgart)">Mercedes-Benz Arena</a> in Bad Cannstatt.</p>
<p>'The Blues', <a href="/wiki/Stuttgarter_Kickers" title="Stuttgarter Kickers">Stuttgarter Kickers</a>, are the second most important football team. They currently play in the <a href="/wiki/Regionalliga_S%C3%BCdwest" title="Regionalliga Südwest">Regionalliga Südwest</a> (fourth division) at the smaller <a href="/wiki/Gazi-Stadion" class="mw-redirect" title="Gazi-Stadion">Gazi Stadium</a> close to the <a href="/wiki/Fernsehturm_Stuttgart" title="Fernsehturm Stuttgart">TV tower</a> in Degerloch.</p>
<p>Other lower-division football teams are <i>Sportfreunde Stuttgart</i> – most famous for taking part in the <a href="/wiki/Sir_Thomas_Lipton_Trophy" title="Sir Thomas Lipton Trophy">Sir Thomas Lipton Trophy</a> in 1908, considered the first <i>World Cup</i><sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">[181]</a></sup> – and FV Zuffenhausen.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_sports">Other sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stuttgart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: Other sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Stuttgart is home to VfL Pfullingen/Stuttgart, a local <a href="/wiki/Team_handball" class="mw-redirect" title="Team handball">handball</a> team that played in the national league from 2001 to 2006 in the <a href="/wiki/Hanns-Martin-Schleyer-Halle" title="Hanns-Martin-Schleyer-Halle">Schleyerhalle</a>. Its three-times German champion women's volleyball team, <a href="/w/index.php?title=CJD_Feuerbach&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="CJD Feuerbach (page does not exist)">CJD Feuerbach</a>, has now stopped playing for financial reasons but there is now Stuttgart Volleyball Club with a women's team in the 2nd southern league.</p>
<p>Stuttgart has two major ice hockey teams. Stuttgart Rebels EC, plays in the "Landesliga" (4th tier) at the Waldau ice rink in Degerloch. The Bietigheim Bissingen Steelers play in the 2nd division of the DEL (DEL2). The Steelers play in the new Ege Trans Arena in Bietigheim.</p>
<p>The strongest local <a href="/wiki/Water_polo" title="Water polo">water polo</a> team is SV Cannstatt, which won the German championship in 2006.</p>
<p>Stuttgart has two <a href="/wiki/American_football" title="American football">American Football</a> teams: the Stuttgart Nighthawks American football team, who play in the Western Europe Pro League, and the <a href="/wiki/Stuttgart_Scorpions" title="Stuttgart Scorpions">Stuttgart Scorpions</a>, who play in <a href="/wiki/Stuttgarter_Kickers" title="Stuttgarter Kickers">Stuttgarter Kickers</a>' <a href="/wiki/Gazi-Stadion" class="mw-redirect" title="Gazi-Stadion">Gazi Stadium</a>.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Australian_Football" class="mw-redirect" title="Australian Football">Australian Football</a> is practiced by the <a href="/wiki/Stuttgart_Emus" title="Stuttgart Emus">Stuttgart Emus</a> – one of only six active teams in Germany. It participates in the <a href="/wiki/Australian_Football_League_Germany" class="mw-redirect" title="Australian Football League Germany">Australian Football League Germany</a> when they play their home games in the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Eberhard-Bauer-Stadion&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Eberhard-Bauer-Stadion (page does not exist)">Eberhard-Bauer-Stadion</a></p>
<p>TC Weissenhof is a Stuttgart-based women's tennis team that has won the German championship four times. Another women's team is TEC Waldau Stuttgart (German champions in 2006).</p>
<p>HTC Stuttgarter Kickers is one of the most successful <a href="/wiki/Field_hockey" title="Field hockey">field hockey</a> clubs in Germany, having won the German championship in 2005 and a European title in 2006.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sporting_events">Sporting events</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stuttgart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: Sporting events">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Stuttgart has a reputation for staging major events, including the <a href="/wiki/1974_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1974 FIFA World Cup">FIFA World Cup 1974</a>, the finals stages of the FIBA <a href="/wiki/EuroBasket_1985" title="EuroBasket 1985">EuroBasket 1985</a>, the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_1988" title="UEFA Euro 1988">UEFA Euro 1988</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/1993_World_Championships_in_Athletics" title="1993 World Championships in Athletics">World Championships in Athletics 1993</a>. It was also one of the twelve host cities of the <a href="/wiki/2006_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2006 FIFA World Cup">FIFA World Cup 2006</a>. Six matches, three of them second round matches, including the 3rd and 4th place playoff, were played at the Gottlieb Daimler Stadium (today <a href="/wiki/Mercedes-Benz_Arena_(Stuttgart)" title="Mercedes-Benz Arena (Stuttgart)">Mercedes-Benz Arena</a>). Stuttgart was also 2007 <a href="/wiki/European_Capital_of_Sport" class="mw-redirect" title="European Capital of Sport">European Capital of Sport</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">[182]</a></sup> hosting events such as the <a href="/wiki/UCI_World_Championships" title="UCI World Championships">UCI World Cycling Championships</a> Road Race and the <a href="/wiki/IAAF_World_Athletics_Final" title="IAAF World Athletics Final">IAAF World Athletics Final</a>.</p>
<p>Other famous sports venues are the Weissenhof tennis courts, where the annual <a href="/wiki/MercedesCup" class="mw-redirect" title="MercedesCup">Mercedes Cup</a> tennis tournament is played, the <a href="/wiki/Porsche_Arena" class="mw-redirect" title="Porsche Arena">Porsche Arena</a> (hosting tennis, basketball and <a href="/wiki/Team_handball" class="mw-redirect" title="Team handball">handball</a>) and the <a href="/wiki/Hanns-Martin-Schleyer-Halle" title="Hanns-Martin-Schleyer-Halle">Schleyerhalle</a> (<a href="/wiki/Boxing" title="Boxing">boxing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Equestrianism" title="Equestrianism">equestrianism</a>/<a href="/wiki/Show_jumping" title="Show jumping">show jumping</a>, gymnastics, <a href="/wiki/Track_cycling" title="Track cycling">track cycling</a> etc.), <a href="/wiki/Scharrena_Stuttgart" title="Scharrena Stuttgart">Scharrena Stuttgart</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="International_relations">International relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stuttgart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=51" title="Edit section: International relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_twin_towns_and_sister_cities_in_Germany" title="List of twin towns and sister cities in Germany">List of twin towns and sister cities in Germany</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Twin_towns_and_sister_cities">Twin towns and sister cities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stuttgart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=52" title="Edit section: Twin towns and sister cities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/India" title="India"><img alt="India" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/41/Flag_of_India.svg/23px-Flag_of_India.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/41/Flag_of_India.svg/35px-Flag_of_India.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/41/Flag_of_India.svg/45px-Flag_of_India.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1350" data-file-height="900" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Mumbai" title="Mumbai">Mumbai</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maharashtra" title="Maharashtra">Maharashtra</a>, India <small><i>(since 1968)</i></small><sup id="cite_ref-Stuttgart_twinning_191-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stuttgart_twinning-191">[183]</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Tunisia" title="Tunisia"><img alt="Tunisia" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Flag_of_Tunisia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Tunisia.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Flag_of_Tunisia.svg/35px-Flag_of_Tunisia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Flag_of_Tunisia.svg/45px-Flag_of_Tunisia.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="800" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Menzel_Bourguiba" title="Menzel Bourguiba">Menzel Bourguiba</a> in Tunisia <small><i>(since 1971)</i></small><sup id="cite_ref-Stuttgart_twinning_191-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stuttgart_twinning-191">[183]</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt"><img alt="Egypt" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Flag_of_Egypt.svg/23px-Flag_of_Egypt.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Flag_of_Egypt.svg/35px-Flag_of_Egypt.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Flag_of_Egypt.svg/45px-Flag_of_Egypt.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Cairo" title="Cairo">Cairo</a>, Egypt <small><i>(since 1979)</i></small><sup id="cite_ref-Stuttgart_twinning_191-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stuttgart_twinning-191">[183]</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland"><img alt="Poland" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/12/Flag_of_Poland.svg/23px-Flag_of_Poland.svg.png" width="23" height="14" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/12/Flag_of_Poland.svg/35px-Flag_of_Poland.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/12/Flag_of_Poland.svg/46px-Flag_of_Poland.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="800" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/%C5%81%C3%B3d%C5%BA" title="Łódź">Łódź</a>, <a href="/wiki/%C5%81%C3%B3d%C5%BA_Voivodeship" title="Łódź Voivodeship">Łódź Voivodeship</a>, Poland <small><i>(since 1988)</i></small><sup id="cite_ref-Stuttgart_twinning_191-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stuttgart_twinning-191">[183]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-.C5.81.C3.B3d.C5.BA_twinning_195-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-.C5.81.C3.B3d.C5.BA_twinning-195">[187]</a></sup></li>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Friendships">Friendships</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stuttgart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=53" title="Edit section: Friendships">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Stuttgart also has <b>special friendships</b> with the following cities:<sup id="cite_ref-Stuttgart_partnerships_197-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stuttgart_partnerships-197">[189]</a></sup></p>
<table class="wikitable">
<tr valign="top">
<td>
<ul>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan"><img alt="Japan" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9e/Flag_of_Japan.svg/23px-Flag_of_Japan.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9e/Flag_of_Japan.svg/35px-Flag_of_Japan.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9e/Flag_of_Japan.svg/45px-Flag_of_Japan.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/%C5%8Cgaki,_Gifu" title="Ōgaki, Gifu">Ōgaki</a> in <a href="/wiki/Gifu_Prefecture" title="Gifu Prefecture">Gifu Prefecture</a>, Japan <small><i>(since 1988)</i></small><sup id="cite_ref-Stuttgart_partnerships_197-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stuttgart_partnerships-197">[189]</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel"><img alt="Israel" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Flag_of_Israel.svg/21px-Flag_of_Israel.svg.png" width="21" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Flag_of_Israel.svg/32px-Flag_of_Israel.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Flag_of_Israel.svg/41px-Flag_of_Israel.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="660" data-file-height="480" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Shavei_Tzion" title="Shavei Tzion">Shavei Zion</a>, Israel<sup id="cite_ref-Stuttgart_partnerships_197-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stuttgart_partnerships-197">[189]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-mann_198-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mann-198">[190]</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/China" title="China"><img alt="China" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Flag_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Flag_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Flag_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China.svg/45px-Flag_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Nanjing" title="Nanjing">Nanjing</a>, People's Republic of China<sup id="cite_ref-Stuttgart_partnerships_197-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stuttgart_partnerships-197">[189]</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia"><img alt="Malaysia" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Flag_of_Malaysia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Malaysia.svg.png" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Flag_of_Malaysia.svg/35px-Flag_of_Malaysia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Flag_of_Malaysia.svg/46px-Flag_of_Malaysia.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="2800" data-file-height="1400" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Kuantan" title="Kuantan">Kuantan</a>, Malaysia<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">[191]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>The city district of <i>Bad Cannstatt</i>, which has the second largest <a href="/wiki/Mineral_water" title="Mineral water">mineral water</a> sources in Europe, has a partnership with:</p>
<ul>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Hungary" title="Hungary"><img alt="Hungary" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Flag_of_Hungary.svg/23px-Flag_of_Hungary.svg.png" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Flag_of_Hungary.svg/35px-Flag_of_Hungary.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Flag_of_Hungary.svg/46px-Flag_of_Hungary.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="600" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/%C3%9Ajbuda" title="Újbuda">Újbuda</a>, the 11th district of <a href="/wiki/Budapest" title="Budapest">Budapest</a>, Hungary,<sup id="cite_ref-.C3.9Ajbuda_twinnings_200-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-.C3.9Ajbuda_twinnings-200">[192]</a></sup> which has the largest mineral water sources in Europe.</li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_residents">Notable residents</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stuttgart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=54" title="Edit section: Notable residents">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_people_from_Stuttgart" title="List of people from Stuttgart">List of people from Stuttgart</a></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="In_popular_culture">In popular culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stuttgart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=55" title="Edit section: In popular culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Gaming">Gaming</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stuttgart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=56" title="Edit section: Gaming">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>In the 2003 video game <i><a href="/wiki/Command_%26_Conquer:_Generals_Zero_Hour" class="mw-redirect" title="Command &amp; Conquer: Generals Zero Hour">Command &amp; Conquer: Generals Zero Hour</a></i>, GLA forces attacked the US base in Stuttgart in their final mission. In the first Chinese mission, the player must reclaim the city from the GLA.<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">[193]</a></sup></li>
<li>The Medic in <a href="/wiki/Valve_Corporation" title="Valve Corporation">Valve</a>'s 2007 <a href="/wiki/First_person_shooter" class="mw-redirect" title="First person shooter">first person shooter</a> game <a href="/wiki/Team_Fortress_2" title="Team Fortress 2">Team Fortress 2</a> is a native of Stuttgart,<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">[194]</a></sup> but was raised in <a href="/wiki/Rottenburg_am_Neckar" title="Rottenburg am Neckar">Rottenburg am Neckar</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">[195]</a></sup></li>
<li>In the 2008 episodic <a href="/wiki/Adventure_game" title="Adventure game">adventure game</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Sam_%26_Max_Beyond_Time_and_Space" title="Sam &amp; Max Beyond Time and Space">Sam &amp; Max Beyond Time and Space</a></i>, the title characters travel through time to Stuttgart to kill a vampire.<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">[196]</a></sup></li>
<li>Reinhardt, one of the tank classes in <a href="/wiki/Blizzard_Entertainment" title="Blizzard Entertainment">Blizzard</a>'s 2016 team based shooter <i><a href="/wiki/Overwatch_(video_game)" title="Overwatch (video game)">Overwatch</a></i>, originates from Stuttgart. Furthermore, the game also features the map Eichenwalde, which is a fictional castle town near the city.<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">[197]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">[198]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Novels">Novels</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stuttgart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=57" title="Edit section: Novels">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>In the 2005 novel <i><a href="/wiki/The_Book_Thief" title="The Book Thief">The Book Thief</a></i>, protagonist Max Vandenburg resides in Stuttgart until his flight later in the book.<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">[199]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="TV_and_Cinema">TV and Cinema</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stuttgart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=58" title="Edit section: TV and Cinema">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>In the 2012 film <i><a href="/wiki/The_Avengers_(2012_film)" title="The Avengers (2012 film)">The Avengers</a></i>, the villain <a href="/wiki/Loki_(comics)" title="Loki (comics)">Loki</a> is tracked to a gala in Stuttgart, where he intends to steal a large quantity of <a href="/wiki/Iridium" title="Iridium">iridium</a> for his schemes. These scenes were actually filmed in <a href="/wiki/Cleveland" title="Cleveland">Cleveland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ohio" title="Ohio">Ohio</a>, and a number of Stuttgart residents noted the errors in the film's depiction of the city.<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">[200]</a></sup></li>
</ul>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stuttgart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=60" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Footnotes">Footnotes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stuttgart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=61" title="Edit section: Footnotes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: lower-alpha;">
<div class="mw-references-wrap">
<ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-10"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-10">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Sixth in Germany behind <a href="/wiki/Munich" title="Munich">Munich</a>, <a href="/wiki/D%C3%BCsseldorf" title="Düsseldorf">Düsseldorf</a>, <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt" title="Frankfurt">Frankfurt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Berlin" title="Berlin">Berlin</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hamburg" title="Hamburg">Hamburg</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Mercer2015_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mercer2015-9">[9]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-12"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-12">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">10th in Europe and third in Germany behind Munich and Berlin.<sup id="cite_ref-2think2015_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2think2015-11">[10]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-32"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-32">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The history of Stuttgart's <a href="/wiki/Coat_of_Arms" class="mw-redirect" title="Coat of Arms">Coat of Arms</a> is long. The <i><a href="/wiki/File:Wolleber_Chorographia_Mh6-1_0091_Wappen.jpg" title="File:Wolleber Chorographia Mh6-1 0091 Wappen.jpg">Chorographia Württemberg</a></i> of <a href="/w/index.php?title=1591_in_Germany&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="1591 in Germany (page does not exist)">1591</a> shows a horse <i>rampant</i> facing <i>sinister</i> on a field <i>argent</i>. <i><a href="/wiki/Siebmachers_Wappenbuch" title="Siebmachers Wappenbuch">Siebmachers Wappenbuch</a></i> of <a href="/w/index.php?title=1605_in_Germany&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="1605 in Germany (page does not exist)">1605</a> (<a href="/wiki/File:Siebmacher225.jpg" title="File:Siebmacher225.jpg">p. 225</a>) has the modern coat of arms, with the horse facing <i>dexter</i>, on a field <i>or</i>. The modern design of this coat of arms dates to <a href="/wiki/1938_in_Germany" title="1938 in Germany">1938</a> (and was also adopted as part of the <a href="/wiki/Porsche" title="Porsche">Porsche</a> logo in 1952).</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-46"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-46">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">This type of sovereign royal duke was known in Germany as a <i><a href="/wiki/Herzog" title="Herzog">Herzog</a></i></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-107"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-107">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Of those, 67.8% of the residential buildings and 75% of the Industrial structures were destroyed.<sup id="cite_ref-GeschStutt4_106-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GeschStutt4-106">[102]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-112"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-112">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">"When French troops occupied Stuttgart – which was meant to form part of the American Zone as the capital of Württemberg – the Americans ordered them to leave. De Gaulle refused, saying he would stay put until the zones were finalized&#160;... The American solution was to offer them some bits of Baden and Württemberg while keeping the lion's share for themselves&#160;... French soldiers' behaviour in Stuttgart, where some 3,000 women and 8 men were raped, was thought to have added to American fury at their overstepping their lines."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMacDonogh2009_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMacDonogh2009-111">[106]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-124"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-124">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Meinhof had by this point already committed suicide via hanging in her cell, 9 May 1976.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-140"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-140">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The nature of Stuttgart's hilly landscape often makes changes in the city's height. By the Neckar, the elevation is about 207&#160;m (679&#160;ft), whereas the typical height atop the <a href="/wiki/Bernhartsh%C3%B6he" title="Bernhartshöhe">Bernhartshöhe</a> is about 549&#160;m (1,801&#160;ft) – something rather unique in large German cities.</span></li>
</ol>
</div>
